古今图书集成医部全录卷四百十七

小儿风寒门

　　　　千金方 【唐　孙思邈】

　　　　　伤寒

　　论曰：小儿未能冒涉霜雪，乃不病伤寒也。大人解脱之，久伤于寒冷，则不论耳。然天行非节之气，其亦得之。有时行疾疫之年，小儿出腹便患斑者也。治其时行节度，故如大人法，但用药分剂少异，药小冷耳。
　　　　小儿直诀 【宋　钱乙】

　　　　　伤风兼变证治

　　伤风贪睡，口中气热，呵欠烦闷，用大青膏发散之。若饮冷不止而善食者，用大黄丸微下之。余不可下。　　伤风手足冷者，脾脏怯也，当以益黄散温脾胃，以大青膏散风邪。　　伤风自利，脾脏虚怯也，亦用益黄散、大青膏；未瘥，用调中丸。有下证用大黄丸，后服温惊丸。　　伤风腹胀，或作喘，脾脏虚也，当先发散仍补脾。　　伤风兼肝则发搐烦闷，兼心则惊不安，兼肺则喘嗽便气，兼脾则困睡，兼肾则目畏明，各随补其母。[1p]

Comprehensive Collection of Medical Books from Ancient and Modern Times, Volume 417

Childhood Wind and Cold

Thousand Gold Prescriptions (Tang dynasty, Sun Simiao)

Febrile Disease

It is said: Children who have not been exposed to frost and snow do not fall ill from febrile diseases. Adults may suffer from cold for a long time, but this is not the concern here. However, when the weather is out of season, children may still become ill. Sometimes, during epidemic years, children can show symptoms like rashes after childbirth. In treating seasonal illnesses, the methods are similar to those for adults, but the doses of medication should be smaller and cooler.

Direct Formula for Children (Song dynasty, Qian Yi)

Treatment for Wind Cold with Variations in Symptoms

When a child has a cold and is overly sleepy with a warm breath and feels uneasy, use large blue ointment to disperse it. If they continuously drink cold water and have a good appetite, use a small dose of rhubarb pills. Other remedies should not be purgative. For cold hands and feet, which indicate spleen deficiency, use nourishing yellow powder to warm the spleen and stomach along with large blue ointment to dispel wind pathogens. If the child is experiencing diarrhea due to a cold and has a weak spleen, use nourishing yellow powder and large blue ointment; if not healed, administer regulating middle pills. For cases of diarrhea, give rhubarb pills, followed later by warming and calming pills. If there is abdominal bloating or wheezing due to a weak spleen, first disperse and then reinforce the spleen. If the cold affects the liver, it will cause convulsions and restlessness; if it affects the heart, there will be anxiety; if it affects the lungs, there will be wheezing and coughing; if it affects the spleen, it will lead to drowsiness; if it affects the kidneys, the child may be sensitive to light. Each condition should be treated based on the organ that is affected.[1p]

　　伤风多睡能食，引饮吐泻，大便色黄，此胃虚热也，当先用白朮散以生津，后用大青膏以发散。　　伤风吐沫，泻色青白，闷乱不渴，哽气出气，睡而露睛，先用益黄散，后用大青膏。　　伤风或凉或热，多睡气粗，大便黄白，呕乳不消，不时咳嗽，先用大青膏，后服益黄散，慎不可下！　　伤风误用下药而作渴饮水者，此胃亡津液而虚热也，多用白朮散，热渴自止。　　 【注　按大青膏乃表散之剂，必外邪蕴结于肺，而肺气未亏损者，方可用之。大黄丸乃疏利之剂，其食痰积滞于胃，而胃气尚充实者，乃可施之。况前证属脾肺气虚，腠理不密，外邪所乘，又当临证制宜，必以固脾胃为主。[2p]

Wind injury leads to excessive sleeping and eating, causing drinking and vomiting, with yellow stools; this indicates deficiency heat in the stomach. First, use Baizhu Powder to generate fluids, then use Daqing Paste to disperse.

With wind injury causing foamy vomiting, blue-white diarrhea, a feeling of distress without thirst, belching, and visible eyes while asleep, first use Yihuang Powder, then Daqing Paste.

With wind injury being hot or cold, excessive sleeping with coarse breathing, yellow-white stools, undigested milk vomiting, and intermittent coughing, first use Daqing Paste, then take Yihuang Powder, but be cautious not to use purgatives!

If purgatives are wrongly used for wind injury, causing thirst and a desire for water, this means the stomach has lost fluids and is in deficiency heat. Use Baizhu Powder frequently, and the heat thirst will naturally cease.

Note: Daqing Paste is a remedy for dispersing exterior pathogens and should only be used when external pathogens have invaded the lungs, but lung qi has not been depleted. Dahuang Pill is a remedy for unblocking and should be applied when phlegm and stagnation accumulate in the stomach, with stomach qi still relatively robust. Moreover, since previous symptoms indicate spleen and lung qi deficiency, with open pores susceptible to external pathogens, treatment must be tailored to the case, primarily focusing on strengthening the spleen and stomach.[2p]

若兼肢冷自利，腹胀喘嗽者，脾肺虚寒也，六君子加木香、升麻、桔梗。若兼惊悸痰甚，饮食少思，属心脾脏虚也，四君子加芎、归、酸枣仁。若兼肢体倦怠，喘嗽哽气，脾肺气虚也，六君子、当归、桔梗。若兼目畏明，白睛多，肾气虚也，六味丸加五味、鹿茸；如未应，更用补中益气汤加五味子、干山药，以补肾母。若多睡能乳，饮水吐泻，大便色黄，脾气虚而下陷也，补中益气汤升补元气。若吐沫泻青，睡而露睛，脾虚木所乘也，六君子加升麻、柴胡，调补脾气。[3p]

If there are cold limbs and self-benefiting, along with abdominal bloating and coughing, this indicates deficiency of the spleen and lungs due to cold. Use Liu Junzi Decoction with added Mu Xiang, Sheng Ma, and Jie Geng. If there are also palpitations and excessive phlegm, with little appetite and concern, this signifies deficiency of the heart and spleen. Use Si Junzi Decoction with added Chuan Xiong, Gui, and Suan Zao Ren. If there is also fatigue in the limbs, coughing, and shortness of breath, indicating qi deficiency of the spleen and lungs, use Liu Junzi Decoction with Dang Gui and Jie Geng. If there is sensitivity to light, with a lot of white sclera, this suggests kidney qi deficiency. Use Liu Wei Di Huang Wan with added Wu Wei Zi and Lu Rong; if not effective, further use Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction with Wu Wei Zi and Shan Yao to nourish the kidney source. If there is excessive sleep and the person exhibits milk-like symptoms, with vomiting water and diarrhea, and yellow stool, this indicates deficiency of spleen qi and sinking down. Use Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction to raise and supplement the original qi. If there is foamy diarrhea and the patient sleeps with open eyes, indicating spleen deficiency due to invasion by wood, use Liu Junzi Decoction with added Sheng Ma and Chai Hu to adjust and supplement the spleen qi.[3p]

若乍凉乍热，喘嗽气粗，大便黄白，呕乳不消，脾肺气虚而有邪也，先用惺惺散，后用四君子汤。若误用下药再作渴者，脾胃之气伤也，用白朮散，或六君子、补中益气二汤补之。大凡前证若病邪急，而元气无亏者，先用原方，或用轻清表散之剂；若元气不足者，当如前法固其元气，则外邪自退；若因病久或因服克伐之药而未愈，或更加变证者，但调补脾胃，诸证自愈。其小儿伤风发热，鼻塞或痰壅发搐，多因乳母鼻吹顖门，但服惺惺膏，或用葱头三五茎，细切擂烂，以纸寸余，摊葱在上，两掌合葱，待温贴于顖门，其邪即解。乃去其葱，却用绢段寸余，涂以面糊，仍贴顖门，永无伤风之患。】[4p]

When one experiences alternating chills and fever, heavy breathing, yellowish-white stools, vomiting undigested milk, and has spleen and lung qi deficiency together with pathogenic factors, first use Xingxing San, followed by Si Junzi Tang. If laxatives are mistakenly used and thirst arises, it indicates damage to the spleen and stomach qi; in this case, use Baizhu San or either Liu Junzi or Buzhong Yiqi Decoction to nourish. Generally, if the aforementioned symptoms appear urgently but the vital energy is intact, first use the original formula or a mild, clearing external remedy; if the vital energy is insufficient, as mentioned earlier, strengthen the vital energy to dispel external pathogens. If due to prolonged illness or the use of depleting medications the condition does not improve or mutates further, simply nourishing the spleen and stomach will lead to self-recovery. For children with wind-cold causing fever, nasal congestion, or phlegm blockage leading to convulsions, this often results from the wet breath of the wet nurse affecting the child’s fontanelle. They should take Xingxing Gao or use three to five stalks of green onions, finely chopped and pounded, spread on a piece of paper an inch long, and applied warm to the fontanelle; the pathogen will then be resolved. After removing the onions, take a silk piece about an inch long, coat it with flour paste, and reapply to the fontanelle, permanently alleviating the risk of catching a cold.[4p]

　　　　婴童百问 【明　鲁伯嗣】

　　　　　伤寒正受伤寒夹惊

　　小儿伤寒，初得浑身发热无汗，多啼哭，看眼急有如惊风，但用发散退热，莫令发渴；如渴便欲饮水不歇，当发散，羌活散、三黄散、柴胡散、抱龙丸；或虚烦，可用竹叶汤。如嫩小儿当服洗心散、薄荷散、红绵散，四肢发汗，自然精神喜悦。感伤寒之重者，当依仲景之法治之。又有伤寒夹惊，先要发散，其热乃退。化痰截惊，乳下婴儿抱龙丸，羌活散加荆芥、防风，三黄散，微利痰热；次用柴胡、黄芩药调理，管取向安。葱白汤方可服。[5p]

Injuries of Cold and Shock

In the case of children with cold injuries, initially, there will be a fever without sweating, and they may cry excessively, appearing startled as if affected by sudden fright. One should use methods to dissipate heat without allowing thirst to develop; if thirst arises, they desire to drink water continuously, which indicates the need for dissipation. Remedies such as Qianghuo Powder, Sanhuang Powder, Chaihu Powder, or Baolong Pill may be used; if there is restlessness, Bamboo Leaf Decoction can be applied. For very young children, they should take Xixing Powder, Mint Powder, or Hongmian Powder, which will induce sweating in the limbs and naturally improve their spirit and mood. For severe cold injuries, treatment should follow the methods of Zhongjing.

When there is cold injury accompanied by shock, the first step is to dissipate the heat. To resolve phlegm and stop the shock, Baolong Pill can be given to infants under a year old, along with Qianghuo Powder combined with Jingjie and Fangfeng, and Sanhuang Powder to help relieve phlegm heat. Next, Chaihu and Huangqin should be used to regulate the condition, ensuring a calming effect. Scallion White Decoction can be administered.[5p]

　　　　　小儿伤寒与时气同异

　　夫小儿伤寒，得之与大人无异，所异治者，兼惊而已。又有因夹惊食而得，治法与大人一同，但小其分剂，使药性少瘥耳。仲景云：春气温和，夏气炎热，秋气清凉，冬气冷冽，此则四时正气之序也。冬时严寒，触冒之者，乃名伤寒耳。其伤于四时之气，皆能为病。冬受寒毒之气，其即时而病者，头痛身疼，肌肤热而恶寒，名曰伤寒，其不即时病者，寒毒藏于肌肤之间，至春夏阳气发生，则寒毒与阳气相搏于荣卫之间，其病与冬时即病无异，但因春而发名曰温病，至夏而发名曰热病。阳热未盛，为寒所制，病名为温；阳热已盛，寒不能制，病名为热。故太医均谓之伤寒也。然热病、伤寒、温病。时气，传变无异也。凡时气者，四时之间有不正之气也。如春应暖而反寒，夏应热而反冷，秋应凉而反热，冬应寒而反温，非其时而有其气。[6p]

Children's Febrile Illness and Seasonal Differences

Children’s febrile illness, whether acquired or experienced by adults, is fundamentally the same; the only difference in treatment is that children may also be startled. It can also arise from being startled while eating. The treatment method is similar to that for adults, but the dosage is smaller, resulting in a milder effect of the medicine. Zhang Zhongjing stated: in spring, the air is warm and gentle; in summer, it is hot and intense; in autumn, it is cool and refreshing; in winter, it is cold and bitter. This is the proper sequence of the four seasonal energies. When winter is harshly cold, those who encounter it are said to suffer from febrile illness. Any adverse effects of the seasonal energies can lead to illness. If one is afflicted by cold toxins in winter, the immediate symptoms include headache, body aches, fever, and chills, termed febrile illness. If symptoms do not appear immediately, the cold toxins may remain hidden in the skin, and as the yang energy rises in spring and summer, these toxins conflict with the yang in the body's protective system, producing a condition similar to the immediate illness experienced in winter, but due to its emergence in spring, it is termed a warm disease, and if it occurs in summer, it is termed a hot disease. When the yang heat is not yet abundant and is restricted by cold, it is called a warm illness; when the yang heat is abundant and cold cannot restrict it, it is called a hot illness. Therefore, the great physicians refer to it as febrile illness. However, hot diseases, febrile illnesses, and warm diseases are all variations of seasonal ailments that can change and intermingle. Seasonal ailments arise from improper experiences of the seasonal energies. For instance, if spring should be warm but is cold instead, summer should be hot but is cold, autumn should be cool but is hot, and winter should be cold but is warm, it is improper for the season to present such energies.[6p]

气之中人，则头疼壮热咳嗽气粗，烦渴心躁，恍忽惊悸，传变与伤寒无异。故一岁之中，病无长少，率相似者，此则时行之气，俗谓之天行是也。治法：三四月或有暴寒，其时阳气尚弱，为寒所折，病热犹轻，升麻汤解肌汤主之。五六月阳气已盛，为寒所折，病热则重；七八月阳气已衰，为寒所折，病热亦微。调中汤、射干汤、半夏桂甘汤可选用也。秋温冬温，治湿则利小便。治冬温亦宜解利。其利小便也，则以五苓散辈；其解利冬温，宜葳蕤汤。盖冬温者，感温气而作。寒疫者，暴寒折人，非触冒之过，其治法不同，所施寒热温凉之剂亦异，不可拘以日数，发汗吐下，随证施行。要之治热以寒，温而行之；治温以清，冷而行之；治寒以热，凉而行之；治清以温，热而行之。以平为期，不可以过，此为大法。汤氏有七宝散，加减服之，并与乳母尤好。有热者，升麻汤加柴胡、黄芩等剂治之，柴胡石膏汤极效。[7p]

In the case of illnesses caused by seasonal influences, symptoms can include headaches, fever, cough, rough breathing, irritability and thirst, a restless heart, confusion, and anxiety, resembling conditions like typhoid. Therefore, throughout the year, one may experience various ailments, which often appear similar; this is known as the seasonal wind or what people refer to as "heavenly influences."

Treatment methods: In March and April, if there is a sudden cold, the yang energy is still weak and can be affected by the cold, leading to milder heat symptoms. In such cases, the Shegan Decoction or Sang Ju San is prescribed. In May and June, as the yang energy increases, if affected by cold, the heat symptoms can become severe; in July and August, as the yang energy declines, the cold can again have a lesser effect. The Tiaozhong Decoction, Shegan Decoction, and Banxia Guizhi Decoction can be selected for use.

In autumn and winter, treatment for dampness is aimed at promoting urination. For winter heat, it is also advisable to relieve and promote urination. For promoting urination, the Wuling San can be used; for relieving winter heat, the Weirui Decoction is appropriate. Winter heat arises from the influence of warm energies. Cold epidemics cause sudden cold effects on people; this is not due to exposure but is treated differently, and the herbs for cold and heat are also different. One should not rigidly adhere to a fixed timeframe for treatment but should adjust sweating, vomiting, or purging according to symptoms.

In summary, to treat heat, use cold methods; to treat warmth, use clearing methods; to treat cold, apply heating methods; to treat clarity, use warm methods. Aim for balance and avoid excess, which is the fundamental principle. The Tang family has the Seven Treasures Powder, which can be adjusted and taken, especially beneficial for nursing mothers. For those with heat symptoms, adding Chai Hu and Huang Qin to the Shegan Decoction is effective, and the Chai Hu Shigao Decoction is particularly potent.[7p]

　　　　　伤寒表里

　　凡治小儿伤寒，须辨表里，表里不分，汗下差误。古人云：桂枝下咽，阳盛即毙；承气入胃，阴盛以亡。伤寒有表证，有里证，有半在表、半在里，有表里二证俱见。然在表者宜汗，在里者宜下，在半表半里者宜和解，表里俱见，随证施治。无表里证，用大柴胡汤下之。其表证者，发热恶寒，身体痛而脉浮，无汗头疼，项强腰脊痛；此足太阳膀胱经受病也，宜汗之。然伤寒发表，当随病轻重而汗之，头疼发热兼惊，亦只用葱白汤汗之，甚则麻黄汤、各半汤、解肌汤、葛根汤、柴胡散，皆可选而用之。[8p]

In treating pediatric typhoid fever, it is essential to distinguish between exterior and interior conditions. Without this distinction, sweating or purging may be misguided. Ancient sages said: "With Gui Zhi, if the Yang is excessive, it leads to death; with Cheng Qi, if the Yin is excessive, it leads to disaster." Typhoid has both exterior symptoms and interior symptoms; some may present as half exterior and half interior, while others may show both conditions at once.

For those with exterior symptoms, sweating is advisable; for those with interior symptoms, purging is appropriate. In cases of mixed symptoms, harmonizing treatment is necessary. If there are no distinct exterior or interior symptoms, administer Da Chai Hu Decoction.

Exterior symptoms include fever, chills, body aches, a floating pulse, lack of sweating, headache, stiffness of the neck, and back pain; these indicate illness of the Tai Yang Bladder channel and should be treated with sweating. However, the method of sweating for exterior symptoms should depend on the severity of the illness. For headaches and fever accompanied by agitation, it may suffice to use Scallion White Decoction for sweating; for more severe cases, options include Ma Huang Decoction, Ge Gen Decoction, Xiao Feng San, and others, which can all be selected for use.[8p]

其里证者，恶热而不恶寒，手掌心并腋下濈濈汗出，胃中干，咽燥，粪结聚，潮热，大便硬，小便如常，腹满而喘，躁渴脉沉而滑，内热而谵语，此属足阳明胃经也，宜下之，小承气汤、大承气汤、四顺饮、洗心散，斟酌轻重用之。其在半表半里者，心下满，口不欲食，大便硬，脉沉细，是里证，当下；其人头汗出，微恶寒，手足冷，即当汗。此两证俱见者，仲景所谓半在表半在里也，小柴胡汤主之。太阳病不解，传入少阳，胁下硬满，干呕不能入饮食，往来寒热，尚未吐下，诊其脉弦紧者，小柴胡汤主之，此属少阳胆经也，宜和解。其表里两证俱见者，病人脉浮而大，是表证，当汗；其人发热烦渴，小便赤，是里证，当下。是表里证俱见，五苓散主之。又伤寒不大便六七日，头痛有热者是也，里证当下；其人小便清者，知不在里，仍在表，当须发汗。[9p]

In cases of interior syndrome, there is a dislike for heat but not for cold, with profuse sweating from the palms and armpits, dryness in the stomach, a dry throat, constipated stools, tidal fever, hard stools, normal urination, a full abdomen with shortness of breath, restlessness and thirst, a deep and slippery pulse, and internal heat causing delirium; this indicates a pattern of the Stomach meridian of the Foot Yangming and should be treated with purgatives such as Xiao Chengqi Decoction, Da Chengqi Decoction, Si Shun Drink, and Xixin Powder, used according to the severity.

In cases that are both half-exterior and half-interior, where there is fullness beneath the heart, lack of appetite, hard stools, and a deep, thin pulse, this is an interior syndrome and should be purged; if the person has sweating on the head, a slight aversion to cold, and cold hands and feet, then sweating should be induced. When both of these syndromes are present, as mentioned by Zhongjing, this is called half in the exterior, half in the interior, and should be treated with Xiao Chaihu Decoction.

In cases of Taiyang disease not resolving and transitioning into Shaoyang, with hardness and fullness beneath the ribs, dry retching unable to accept food and drink, and alternating chills and fever, if the pulse is taut and tight, then Xiao Chaihu Decoction is indicated, as this pertains to the Shaoyang Gallbladder meridian, and harmonization is necessary.

If both exterior and interior symptoms are present, and the patient has a floating and large pulse, this indicates an exterior syndrome, and sweating should be applied; if the person has fever, thirst, and red urination, this indicates an interior syndrome, and purgation is necessary. Thus, in cases where both exterior and interior symptoms appear together, Wu Ling San is the appropriate treatment.

Furthermore, if a person with a fever has not defecated for six or seven days and has a headache with heat, this indicates an interior syndrome that should be purged; if the person’s urination is clear, it shows that the condition is still in the exterior, and sweating must be induced.[9p]

此是两证俱见，即未可下，宜与桂枝汤。又太阳病医反下之，因亦腹痛，是有表复有里，仲景用桂枝加芍药汤，痛甚者桂枝加大黄汤；或腹满时痛，尺寸脉俱浮洪者，此足太阴脾经也，自利不渴当温之，四逆汤理中汤。其无表里者，伤寒四五日以后，以至过经无表里证，又于里证未可下者，既非下证，亦非汗证，皆可用小柴胡汤随证加减用之。以至十余日外用小柴胡汤不愈者，若大便硬，看可下，则用大柴胡汤下之。仲景云：六七日目中不了了，睛不和，无表里证，大便难，身微热，此为实也，当下，宜大承气汤。若不渴口不燥，舌干而脉沉者，急温之，宜四逆汤。此足少阴肾经也。[10p]

This indicates that both symptoms are present; therefore, it is not appropriate to purge. It is advisable to use Gui Zhi Decoction. Furthermore, in cases of Taiyang disease, if the physician purges, and there is also abdominal pain, this indicates an exterior condition combined with an interior condition. Zhang Zhongjing employed Gui Zhi Decoction with Shao Yao. If the pain is severe, Gui Zhi Decoction with Da Huang is used; or if the pain occurs when the abdomen is distended and both pulse readings are floating and surging, this corresponds to the Foot Taiyin Spleen Meridian. If there is free bowel movement and no thirst, it should be warmed with Si Ni Decoction or Li Zhong Decoction. If there are no exterior or interior symptoms after four or five days of febrile disease and the case has exceeded the time without exterior or interior symptoms, and if there are still interior symptoms that should not be purged, these cases are neither purging nor sweating conditions, and Xiao Chai Hu Decoction can be used, adjusting according to symptoms. If after ten days of using Xiao Chai Hu Decoction there is no improvement, if the stools are hard and purging is deemed necessary, then Da Chai Hu Decoction should be used to purge them. Zhang Zhongjing states that if after six or seven days the eyes are unclear, the vision is not harmonious, and there are no exterior or interior symptoms, with difficult stool and slight feverishness of the body, this signifies a solid condition, and it should be purged using Da Cheng Qi Decoction. If there is no thirst, the mouth is not dry, but the tongue is dry and the pulse is deep, urgent warming is required, suggesting Si Ni Decoction is appropriate. This pertains to the Foot Shaoyin Kidney Meridian.[10p]

其表热里寒者，身大热而反欲得衣，热在皮肤，寒在骨髓也，宜先与阴旦汤；塞已，次以小柴胡汤加桂，以温其表。又身大寒而反不欲近衣，寒在皮肤，热在骨髓也，宜先与白虎加人参汤；热除，次以桂枝麻黄各半汤以解其外。又厥阴证脉浮缓者，必囊不缩，外证必发热恶寒似疟，为欲愈，宜桂枝麻黄各半汤。若脉尺寸俱沉短者，必囊缩，毒气入脏，宜承气汤下之。厥阴病，其脉微浮为欲愈，不浮为未愈，宜小建中汤，此足厥阴肝经也。然以表里证内近似三阴三阳之证，而疏于各证之下，非可以尽备六经之大法也，当以《活人书》、《伤寒论》为主。其疟证与大方治法同，后有本条。夏伤于暑，秋必痎疟。其暑证玉露散主之，其详亦与大方同其治法，但用分剂轻耳。《口议》有脱甲散，大能除热，扶表救里，真良方也！[11p]

If the surface is hot and the interior is cold, the body feels very hot and desires clothing; the heat is on the skin and the cold in the bone marrow. One should first administer Yindan Decoction; after alleviating this, follow with Xiao Chai Hu Decoction with added cinnamon to warm the surface. If the body feels very cold and desires no clothing, the cold is on the skin and the heat in the bone marrow. One should first administer Bai Hu Decoction with added ginseng; after eliminating the heat, follow with a decoction of equal parts cinnamon twig and ephedra to ease the exterior.

For the condition of Jueyin, where the pulse is floating and weak, the bag must not contract, and the exterior symptoms must feature fever and chills resembling malaria, indicating a desire for recovery. Therefore, one should use a decoction of equal parts cinnamon twig and ephedra. If the pulse at both positions is deep and short, the bag must contract, indicating that toxic qi has entered the organs; one should use Chengqi Decoction to purge it.

In Jueyin disease, if the pulse is slightly floating this indicates a desire for recovery; if not floating, recovery is not yet achieved. In this case, Xiao Jian Zhong Decoction should be used, as this pertains to the Jueyin liver channel. However, exterior and interior conditions may resemble the three Yin and three Yang syndromes, and should not be hastily categorized under the six major patterns of disease. Therefore, one should refer primarily to the "Book of Living Persons" and "Discussion on Cold Damage."

The malaria signs follow the same treatment as in major treatises, with further details in this section. Summer heat-related issues will certainly lead to chills and fevers in the autumn. Treatments for heat conditions are primarily based on Yulu Powder, and the specifics of its healing method are similar to those in major treatises, albeit using lighter dosages. "Oral Discussions" mention Tie Jia San, which is very effective in dispelling heat, supporting the surface, and rescuing the interior; truly a fine remedy![11p]

　　　　　伤寒咳嗽伤风

　　仲阳云：咳嗽者，肺感微寒，八九月间肺气大旺，病嗽者其病必实，非久病也，其证面赤，身热痰盛，法当以葶苈丸下之；若久嗽，不可下也。冬月嗽，乃伤风咳也，当以麻黄汤汗之；有热证面赤饮水，涎痰浓稠，咽喉不利者，宜甘桔汤；有肺盛者嗽而后喘，面肿欲饮水，有不饮水者，其身即热，以泻白散泻之；有嗽而吐涎痰，乳食者，以白饼子下之。然肺主气，应于皮毛，肺为五脏华盖，小儿感于风寒，客于皮肤，入伤肺经，微者咳嗽，重者喘急。肺伤于寒则嗽，多痰涎，喉中鸣急，肺伤于暖，则嗽声不通雍滞。伤于寒者必散寒邪，伤于暖者必泄壅滞。发散属以甘辛，即桂枝、麻黄、细辛是也；涌泄系以酸苦，即葶苈、大黄是也。更五味子、乌梅之酸，可以敛肺气，亦治咳嗽之要药也，久嗽不已，必生惊悸顽涎，血脉灌脸。[12p]

Cold-induced Cough and Wind

Zhong Yang said: In cases of cough, the lungs are slightly affected by cold. In the months of August and September, the lung qi is vigorous; those who suffer from cough in this period must have a substantial illness, not due to a long-standing condition. The symptoms include a flushed face, body heat, and abundant phlegm, which should be treated with Ting Li Wan. However, if the cough has persisted for a long time, it should not be purged.

In winter, cough is due to a wind cold, which should be treated with Ma Huang Tang to induce sweating. If there is a red face, drinking water, and thick phlegm with an obstructed throat, Gan Ju Tang should be used. In cases where lung qi is high leading to coughing and then wheezing, with facial swelling and a desire to drink water, but the person refrains, their body is definitely hot, and Bai Shao San should be used to purge it. If there is coughing with expectoration of phlegm, and a diet of milk or dairy, then Bai Bing Zi should be administered.

The lungs govern qi and are related to the skin and hair; they are the protective cover of the five zang organs. Young children affected by wind and cold, as it gets to their skin, can harm the lung channels, causing mild coughing or severe wheezing. If the lungs are injured by cold, there will be a cough with abundant phlegm, and a rapid sound in the throat. If injured by warmth, then the cough will be congested and obstructed.

Cold-induced injuries require expelling the cold pathogens, while warmth-induced injuries require draining the obstruction. To disperse cold, use sweet and pungent herbs like Gui Zhi, Ma Huang, and Xi Xin; for draining, use sour and bitter herbs like Ting Li and Da Huang. Additionally, the sourness of Wu Mei and Wu Wei Zi can help restrain lung qi and are vital medicines for treating cough. If a cough persists, it will definitely lead to a sensation of fright, stubborn phlegm, and blood vessels bursting in the face.[12p]

其嗽传受五脏，或吐逆，或痰涎，或厥冷，或恐悸，甚而至于眼目两眶，紫黑如被物伤损，眼白红赤如血。谓之血眼。治之之法、当用生地黄及湿黑豆研成膏，掩眼上，而眼肿黑自消，其血皆自眼泪而出，真良方也。兼服麦煎散而嗽自止。久嗽成癎，当服散癎等剂。凡治嗽先要发散寒邪，然后服宽气化痰止嗽之药，即得痊瘥。先服九宝丸、华盖散、葶苈丸、抱龙丸，或细辛五味子汤；如有热可服凉肺之药，柴胡、黄芩等剂，并泻白散；痰多气喘，用金星丸；利痰了，却服前药，后服百部丸、生犀散、天麻定喘饮，调理而安。冷证咳嗽，小青龙汤加杏仁，去麻黄，亦可服。有热及时气咳嗽，柴胡散加杏仁、五味子，柴胡石膏汤亦可，钱氏生犀散加减亦佳。有惊咳嗽，天麻防风丸治之。惺惺散、化风丹皆可服。金沸草散、三拗汤加减，乃治伤风咳嗽之常剂也。和解汤治四时感冒，可加减服。[13p]

Coughing affects the five internal organs; it may result in reverse flow, phlegm and drool, coldness, or palpitations. In severe cases, the area around the eyes can become purple and black as if injured, with the whites of the eyes appearing red like blood. This is referred to as "blood eyes." The method of treatment involves using raw Rehmannia and moist black beans ground into a paste and applied over the eyes. The swelling and darkness will reduce, and blood will flow out as tears, truly an excellent remedy. Additionally, taking wheat decoction powder will help stop the cough.

If the cough has persisted for a long time and has become a chronic condition, one should take powder to treat the syndrome. Generally, in treating a cough, one must first dispel the cold pathogen, then take medicine to relieve phlegm and stop the cough to achieve recovery. One should first take Nine Treasure Pills, Huagai Powder, Tingli Pills, or Baolong Pills; or a decoction of Chuanxiong and Schisandra. If there is heat, cooling herbs for the lung such as Chaihu and Huangqin can be employed, along with Baihua Powder; if there is abundant phlegm and shortness of breath, use Jinxing Pills. When phlegm is cleared, return to the previous remedies, then take Baibu Pills, Shengxi Powder, and Tianma Decoction to regulate and stabilize.

For cough due to cold, Xiao Qinglong Decoction plus apricot kernels, excluding ephedra, is also appropriate. For cough due to heat and timely Qi, Chaihu Powder with apricot kernels and Schisandra or Chaihu Shigao Decoction may also be good. Modified Qian's Shengxi Powder works well too. For cough due to fright, Tianma Fangfeng Pills are effective. Both Xingxing Powder and Huafeng Dan are applicable. Jinfencao Powder and San'ao Decoction, with adjustments, are common remedies for cough from a cold. Hejie Decoction can be taken for colds at any time of the year, with adjustments as necessary.[13p]

　　　　明医杂着 【明　王纶】

　　　　　伤风流涕

　　小儿八岁以下，无伤寒，虽有感冒伤风，鼻塞流涕，发热咳嗽，以降痰为主，略加微解。凡散利败毒，非幼稚所宜。感冒轻者不必用药，候二三日多有自愈。　　 【注　按前证，若手足冷或腹胀，脾虚也，用六君子汤加升麻、柴胡；若腹胀或气喘，肺虚也，用四君子汤加柴胡、升麻。经云：肺主气而司皮毛，肺虚则腠理不密，外邪易感。凡发表之后，其邪既去，用补脾肺以实其表，庶风邪不能再入；往往表散之后，热嗽不退，复行发表，多变坏证。】[14p]

Ming Medical Miscellany
Ming Dynasty - Wang Lun

Wind Injury and Runny Nose

For children under eight years old, without signs of a cold, even if they have symptoms such as nasal congestion, runny nose, fever, and cough due to a cold, the focus should be on reducing phlegm, with slight relief. Remedies that disperse and eliminate pathogens are not suitable for the young. For mild colds, there is no need for medication, as many tend to recover on their own within two or three days.

Note: If there are signs such as cold hands and feet or abdominal distension, which indicate spleen deficiency, use "Six Gentleman Decoction" with the addition of Sheng Ma and Chai Hu; if there is abdominal distension or shortness of breath indicating lung deficiency, use "Four Gentleman Decoction" with Chai Hu and Sheng Ma. The classics state: "The lungs govern Qi and control the skin and hair. If the lungs are deficient, the pores are not tight, making it easy to be affected by external pathogens." After dispersing the exterior, once the pathogen is eliminated, it is important to tonify the spleen and lungs to consolidate the exterior, preventing the wind pathogen from re-entering; often, after dispersing the exterior, if heat cough persists, repeating exterior dispersal can lead to complications.[14p]

　　　　古今医统 【明　徐春甫】

　　　　　伤寒候

　　小儿伤寒，与大人无异，所以异者，兼有夹食而已。而或偶而中伤，谓之时气，又与伤寒不同。若小儿在襁褓中，或长成而禀赋怯弱，多因乳母解脱衣服，不避风寒所致也。然小儿患此，口不能言其致病之由，脉不能诊其必然之理，但只烦啼发热而已，故不可不尽心焉。初得之时，婴幼则以虎口三关脉纹红色验之，长而童稚，则以一指按其三部，据左手脉之紧盛而断之。其喘急憎寒，心气热，呵欠烦闷，项急者是也。其恶寒恶风，必偎人藏身，引衣密隐，是为表证。恶热内实者，必出头露面，扬手掷足，烦渴燥粪，掀衣气粗，是为里证。至若头额冷汗，手足凉，口冷气，面色黑暗淡，大便泻青，此为阴证。视其小便或赤或白，可以知里热之有无；或青或浊，可以知里证之轻重。举是观之，则汗下清温之法，可类推矣。[15p]

Ancient and Modern Medical System
Ming - Xu Chunfu

On Febrile Diseases in Children

Febrile diseases in children are no different from those in adults; the distinction lies primarily in their susceptibility to improper feeding. Sometimes, they may suffer from external influences known as seasonal afflictions, which are different from mere febrile illnesses. If an infant is weak or has a frail constitution, it is often due to the wet nurse neglecting to keep them warm and exposing them to cold winds. However, children cannot articulate the reasons for their ailments, nor can their pulses reveal clear diagnoses; they only show signs of irritability and fever, which necessitates careful attention.

At the onset of illness, for infants, the redness of the pulse at the tiger's mouth and the three positions can be examined. For older children, one should press one finger on the three levels and determine the condition by assessing the tightness and fullness of the pulse in the left hand. Symptoms include wheezing, fear of cold, heat in the chest, yawning, irritability, and stiffness of the neck. If they show aversion to cold winds and seek warmth, huddling close to others and keeping their bodies covered, these are considered exterior symptoms.

If they have internal heat, they will seek to expose their heads and limbs, showing restlessness, thirst, dryness in stools, and a tendency to throw off their coverings. This indicates interior symptoms. On the other hand, if there is cold sweat on the forehead, coolness in the hands and feet, a cold mouth, dark and pale complexion, and dark diarrhea, this is indicative of a yin condition. Observing the urine, whether red or white, can indicate the presence of internal heat; if it is dark or turbid, this reveals the severity of the internal condition.

From these observations, one may deduce the appropriate method of inducing sweating and using warm remedies.[15p]

　　　　证治准绳 【明　王肯堂】

　　　　　小儿伤寒表里攻发

　　有表证恶风恶寒者，当发。
　　海藏云：恶风者白朮散，恶寒者神朮汤。　　如气盛能食，不大便，无表证者，可攻里。　　春主温属木，身温当发汗。
　　海藏云：神朮汤。
　　夏主长属火，身热而烦躁，合大发散。　　海藏云：神朮加黄芪汤。[16p]

Principles of Diagnosis and Treatment
(Ming Dynasty, Wang Kengtang)

Treatment of Pediatric Typhoid Fever - Exterior and Interior Assault

If there are exterior symptoms of severe wind and severe cold, then it should be released.
Hai Zang says: Severe wind corresponds to Baizhu Powder, severe cold corresponds to Shenjue Decoction. If the energy is strong and the child can eat, but does not have a bowel movement and lacks exterior symptoms, then one may attack the interior.
Spring is associated with warmth and belongs to wood; if the body feels warm, one should induce sweating.
Hai Zang says: Shenjue Decoction.
Summer is associated with growth and belongs to fire; if the body is hot and agitated, it is appropriate to induce great sweating.
Hai Zang says: Shenjue Decoction with Huangqi.[16p]

　　长夏主化属土，及居四季同，当调其饮食。　　海藏云：四君子汤。
　　秋主收属金，身凉内温，合微下。
　　海藏云：通膈丸、金花丸。
　　冬主藏属水，身热而恶寒，是热在外而寒在内；身寒而恶热，是热在内而寒在外。　　海藏云：热在内者，调胃承气汤；寒在内者，调中汤丸。　　有表证恶风恶寒者，当发。
　　凡伤寒，宜依四时阴阳、升降、逆顺、刚柔而施治法。气升浮则顺发之；收藏则下之。有汗发热恶风，脉沉缓者，风伤卫，桂枝汤。　　无汗，发热恶寒，不当风而自憎寒，脉浮紧者，寒伤荣，麻黄汤。　　有汗，发热恶风，脉浮紧，无汗，发热恶寒，脉浮缓，谓之荣卫俱伤，青龙、桂枝麻黄各半汤。　　无汗发热，不恶风寒，脉沉洪者，可下之。更详认其厥与不厥，量寒热深浅而治之。　　有汗，四肢厥，脉沉微者，名阴厥，四逆汤。　　无汗，四肢厥，脉沉微者，名阳厥，大承气汤加腻粉。[17p]

In the long summer, the governing element is earth, and during all four seasons one should adjust their diet. The text mentions: Four Gentlemen Decoction.

In autumn, the governing element is metal; the body is cool and internally warm, which should be slightly lowered. The text mentions: Tonggewan and Jinhua Wan.

In winter, the governing element is water; the body is warm but dislikes cold, indicating heat on the outside and cold on the inside; if the body is cold and dislikes heat, then it suggests heat on the inside and cold on the outside. The text mentions: For heat inside, use the Adjusting Stomach and Chengqi Decoction; for cold inside, use the Adjusting Middle Decoction Pills. If there are exterior symptoms of aversion to wind and cold, one should induce sweating.

In general, for cold damage, one should base treatment on the four seasons of yin and yang, the ascending and descending, and the opposites of rigid and soft. If qi is rising and floating, it should be treated by allowing it to release; if it is stored, it should be lowered. If there is sweating with fever and aversion to wind, along with a deep and slow pulse, this indicates wind injury to the defensive qi, for which one should use Gui Zhi Decoction.

If there is no sweating, with fever and aversion to cold, not being aversive to wind but instead hating cold, and with a floating and tight pulse, this indicates cold injury to the nutritive qi, for which one should use Ma Huang Decoction.

If there is sweating, with fever and aversion to wind, and a floating and tight pulse; or if there is no sweating, with fever and aversion to cold, and a floating and slow pulse, this indicates both the nutritive and defensive qi are injured, so one can use a combination of Qinglong and Gui Zhi Ma Huang Decoction in equal parts.

If there is no sweating and fever, not aversive to wind or cold, and a deep and surging pulse, this can be treated with purgation. The treatment should be more carefully adjusted based on the severity of the cold or heat.

If there is sweating with cold limbs and a deep and weak pulse, this is called yin collapse, for which one would use Si Ni Decoction. If there is no sweating, with cold limbs and a deep and weak pulse, this is called yang collapse, for which one would use the Great Purgative Decoction with the addition of nèi fěn (sticky powder).[17p]

　　如四肢不厥，身热内外皆阳，不动三焦，宜凉药三五服下之。黄芩甘草汤、黄芩白朮汤、黄芩苍朮汤、黄芩栀子汤、连翘饮子、小柴胡汤、八正散、凉膈散、白虎汤、五黄散，此上中下三焦药，宜选用之。　　中暑脉虚。背恶寒自汗而渴者，白虎汤。　　身凉脉紧，热在内者，急下之。口燥咽干，不大便是。　　无汗，身大热者，可发汗，升麻汤、大青膏、天麻膏。　　有汗，身大热者，桂枝汤、惺惺散、解肌汤、小柴胡汤、白朮防风汤，可选用之。　　发汗者，量四时暄暑燥湿风寒，各宜春凉，夏寒、秋温、冬热而发之。[18p]

If the limbs are not cool, and the body is hot both internally and externally, without affecting the three yang organs, it is appropriate to take cooling medicine in doses of three to five. Suitable prescriptions include Huangqin and Gancao Decoction, Huangqin and Baizhu Decoction, Huangqin and Cangzhu Decoction, Huangqin and Ziziphus Decoction, Lianqiao Yinzi, Xiaochaihu Decoction, Bazheng San, Lianggexi San, Baihu Decoction, and Wuhuang San—these are medicines suitable for the upper, middle, and lower jiao.

For heatstroke with a weak pulse, where there is coldness in the back, spontaneous sweating, and thirst, Baihu Decoction is indicated.

If the body feels cool and the pulse is tight, indicating internal heat, it should be urgently purged. If there is dry mouth and throat without bowel movement, it means.

If there is no sweat but great heat in the body, one may induce sweating with Shengma Decoction, Daqing Gao, or Tianma Gao.

If there is sweating with great heat in the body, suitable options include Guizhi Decoction, Xingseng San, Jiemai Decoction, Xiaochaihu Decoction, and Baizhu and Fangfeng Decoction.

For those inducing sweat, it is important to consider the seasonal variations of heat, dryness, dampness, wind, and cold, with appropriate treatments for spring coolness, summer cold, autumn warmth, and winter heat.[18p]

　　　　小儿卫生总微论方 【宋，撰人未详】
　　　　　伤寒论

　　经曰：伤寒者有五，有中风，有热病，有温病，有中湿，有伤寒，其所苦各不同。此五者配入五气，随四时为病。故春风、夏热、秋湿、冬寒、中温，而伤寒则居一焉。其细论在伤寒类证集中。其四时之病、皆谓之伤寒者，乃总概之名也。内热病者，乃盛暑之时，炎热之气中人为病也，又名中暍。湿病者，乃雨露霜雾烟岚水渍湿气中人为病也。小儿无此二病，谓小儿不治家事，未有干办，早卧晚起，不致冲冒故也。外伤风、伤寒、温病，小儿有此三病，谓严寒、厉风、温气无所不至，小儿肌肉脆软，气血柔弱，易为伤之故也。是三病者，其证其脉，不可诊切；儿稍大者，可切脉而别之。[19p]

Treatise on Pediatric Hygiene - On Febrile Illness

The classic text states: There are five types of febrile illnesses: stroke, heat diseases, warm diseases, dampness diseases, and cold diseases, each causing different suffering. These five align with the five energies and correspond to the four seasons for diseases. Thus, spring corresponds to wind, summer to heat, autumn to dampness, winter to cold, and the central season to warmth, with cold residing in one category. Detailed discussions can be found in the classifications of febrile illnesses. The diseases of the four seasons, all referred to as cold illnesses, are general terms.

Internal heat diseases occur during the height of summer, caused by exposure to hot and humid air, also known as "heatstroke." Damp diseases arise from exposure to rain, dew, frost, mist, smoke, and moisture. Young children are not subject to these two forms of illness because they do not engage in household chores, do not become fatigued, and tend to go to bed early and rise late, avoiding excessive exposure.

Young children can suffer from three illnesses: wind, cold, and warm diseases due to severe cold, strong winds, and pervasive warm air. Children's muscles are delicate, and their qi and blood are weak, making them easily injured. For these three diseases, diagnosis through pulse examination is not viable; slightly older children can have their pulses checked for diagnosis.[19p]

伤风之脉阳浮而阴弱也；伤寒之脉，阴阳俱盛而紧濇也；温病之脉，行在诸经，未知何经之动，随其经之所在而取之也。若婴小未能诊切者，但看其形候耳。　　伤风者，乃四时八方为厉之风伤人，其候昏睡，呵欠烦闷，口中气热，或自汗恶风，发热，鼻鸣干呕，热多寒少，面光而不惨，手足皆热，烦躁，治当发散。有饮水者，有能食者，有不能食者。其饮水能食者，可微下之，余不可下也。　　伤寒者，乃冬时严寒之气伤人，入于腠理，当是之时，壮者气行而已，怯者则着而为病。其即发者为伤寒。至春发者为温病。一云在夏至之前，非时行温气之病。夏发者为热病。一云在夏至之后，非中暍之热病。[20p]

The pulse in a case of wind injury is floating in the yang and weak in the yin; the pulse in a case of cold injury has both yin and yang flourishing but is tight and thick; the pulse in a case of warm disease moves through various meridians, and it is unknown which meridian is affected, so the pulse is taken according to where it is located. If a child is too young to be diagnosed through pulse taking, one should observe their physical condition.

Wind injury refers to the harmful winds of all seasons and directions that affect people, presenting symptoms of drowsiness, yawning, irritability, hot breath, occasional sweating with aversion to wind, fever, nasal congestion with dry retching, more heat than cold, a radiant but not pale face, and heat in the hands and feet, alongside restlessness. The treatment should be dispersive. Some can drink water and eat, while others cannot eat. Those who can drink and eat may be treated with gentle purging; the rest should not be purged.

Cold injury, on the other hand, is caused by the severe cold air of winter that harms individuals by penetrating the skin. At that time, robust individuals merely experience qi movement, while the weak develop illness. The immediate onset of this condition is termed cold injury. If it occurs in spring, it is termed warm disease. One might also say that if it occurs before the summer solstice, it is not a seasonal warm disease. If it occurs in summer, it is classified as a heat disease; if after the summer solstice, it is not due to heatstroke.[20p]

其候面赤，浑身壮热，头痛体疼，鼻塞声重，清涕咳嗽，寒毛立，气促急，或呕吐白水，寒多热少，面色惨而不舒，手足指末微冷，不烦躁而恶寒。　　伤风者不恶寒而恶风，伤寒者不恶风而恶寒。其恶风者当风而乃憎寒也；其恶寒者，虽不当风而亦自憎寒也。以此别之。　　治者：若脉洪盛，身体壮热，头痛面赤，四肢暖者，为阳证，宜汗之；若脉微细，身冷，不甚头痛，体疼面青，四肢冷者，为阴证，宜温之。　　温病者，四时之间非节候邪气伤人，如春应温而反寒，夏应热而反冷，秋应凉而反热，冬应寒而反温，言此时通行此气，为病无少长略同，故名天行时气，又名时行温病。[21p]

When the patient’s face is red, the body feels hot, there is headache and body ache, nasal congestion with a heavy voice, clear nasal discharge and cough, hairs standing on end, shortness of breath, possible vomiting of white fluid, predominance of cold over heat, pale and uncomfortable complexion, fingers and toes slightly cold, not irritable yet feeling cold.

Those with wind-cold do not dislike cold but dislike wind; those with cold-illness do not dislike wind but dislike cold. The one who dislikes wind feels cold when exposed to it; the one who dislikes cold may also feel cold even without exposure to wind. This distinguishes between the two.

For treatment: If the pulse is vigorous and strong, body feels hot, headache and face are red, and the limbs are warm, it indicates a yang condition; sweating is advisable. If the pulse is weak and thin, body feels cold, there is not much headache, body aches, face is pale, and the limbs are cold, it indicates a yin condition; warming is advisable.

In cases of warm-illness, if one suffers from unseasonable pathogens, such as feeling cold in spring when it should be warm, or feeling cool in summer when it should be hot, or feeling hot in autumn when it should be cool, or feeling warm in winter when it should be cold, it indicates that these conditions are due to pathogenic qi prevailing at that time. Therefore, this illness has no significant variations, hence termed seasonal pathogenic warm-illness, also known as timely warm-illness.[21p]

其候头痛身重，壮热体疼，与伤寒相似，但临时看其脉与其证，以属何经受病，随经而求之为治也。已上三病，通以伤寒为治。邪在外者解之汗之，邪在内者温之下之，当随证按法而行之。钱乙言伤寒男体重面黄，女喘急面赤，各憎寒，口中气热，呵欠烦闷项急，此乃不分伤风伤寒而概言之也。况伤风伤寒，证候传变多端，自有专经可凭。孙真人云：治小儿与大人无异，惟减用汤剂极少耳。更有伤风寒而兼食者，俗呼谓之夹食伤寒也。其候壮热烦渴，鼻塞声重，四肢困倦，眼黄，腹中胀痛，涎唾呕逆，或呵欠烦闷。治者不先攻所伤，但先解表，候表解然后下之，则病与食皆去也；若不顾其表，便以药攻之，多致结痞也。[22p]

When the patient presents with a headache, heaviness in the body, strong fever, and body aches, it resembles typhoid fever. However, by observing the pulse and symptoms, one must determine which meridian is affected by the illness and treat according to that meridian. The three conditions mentioned above are all treated as if they were typhoid fever. If the pathogen is external, it should be released through sweating; if it is internal, it should be warmed and purged. Treatment should be carried out according to the symptoms and established methods. Qian Yi mentioned that for men suffering from typhoid, the body is heavy and the face is yellow; for women, there is rapid breathing and a red face, both despising cold, with hot breath in the mouth, frequent yawning, and feelings of restlessness. This description does not differentiate between cold and typhoid but addresses them generally. Furthermore, cold and typhoid have multiple variations in symptoms, and there are established methods for each specific condition. Master Sun stated that the treatment for children and adults is no different, except that the quantity of medicinal decoctions should be reduced significantly. There are also cases of cold combined with food intake, commonly referred to as "combined food and typhoid." The symptoms include strong fever, thirst, nasal congestion, heavy voice, fatigue in the limbs, yellowing of the eyes, abdominal distension and pain, salivation, vomiting, or yawning and restlessness. In treatment, one should not first attack the site of injury but rather release the exterior. Once the exterior is resolved, one can then address the internal issues, and both the illness and the food problems will subside; if one disregards the exterior and directly attacks with medicine, it can lead to stagnation and pain.[22p]

又有因失饥而食寒饮冷，伤于脾胃而中风寒，其候胸膈不快，腹胀而痛，面色唇口皆青，手足逆冷，脉沉细者，此寒伤于脾，浸属太阴。庸工不识，以为胸膈不快，妄用针灸，或便投驶药，则胸膈愈不快而吐利，只一两日间便致危殆，此不明之误，非其治也。所谓伤寒本经药证甚多，难以具述。今采其小儿常所患者之方，及有兼见之证，略为条叙。伤风寒手足冷身热面赤头痛者，此脾怯也，宜先和脾，然后发散。伤风寒自利者，脾虚也，宜先补脾，然后发散。未瘥者先调顺其中，有下证者微下之，有惊者退之。　　伤风腹胀而喘者，脾虚也，宜先补脾，去胀定喘；候喘定，然后发散。[23p]

When one suffers from hunger and consumes cold food and drinks, it harms the spleen and stomach, leading to a cold invasion. The signs include discomfort in the chest, abdominal distension and pain, a pale complexion with bluish lips, cold extremities, and a deep, fine pulse. This indicates cold injury to the spleen, belonging to the Taiyin category. Inexperienced practitioners misdiagnose this as simple discomfort in the chest and rashly resort to acupuncture or laxatives, which only worsen the discomfort leading to vomiting and diarrhea. Within just a couple of days, this can result in a critical condition, which reflects a lack of understanding in treatment.

There are many medicinal signs in the classic texts for cold injury, which are difficult to fully describe. Here, I will summarize common cases seen in children and those with overlapping symptoms. For those experiencing cold-induced symptoms like cold hands and feet, fever, reddened face, and headache—this indicates a weak spleen, and one should first harmonize the spleen before dispersing the cold. For those with cold-induced diarrhea, this indicates spleen deficiency, and one should first tonify the spleen before dispersing the cold. If the illness is not yet resolved, one must first regulate the internal condition. If there are signs of diarrhea, one may use mild purging; if there's shock, one should calm it.

For cold-induced abdominal distension accompanied by wheezing, this indicates spleen deficiency, and one should first strengthen the spleen to relieve distension and stabilize breathing. Once the breathing is stable, then one may disperse the cold.[23p]

　　伤风寒得下后，大热已退而余热未解者，是下之太过，胃虚而热乘之故也。胃中虚热者，虽是无多，当生胃中津液，津液得生则热自退矣。　　伤风寒其热在外者为表病，若未入于里，两解之。夫里虚气逆，热结胸中坚硬而痛者，此为结胸；若但硬满而不痛者，此为痞气；若因饮水得者，则为水结。若三四日外热入于里，则腹满痞，内实有燥粪者，当下之。若热入大肠则为大便结濇不通，若热入小肠则为小便难濇不通，热入大小肠则为大小便不通。热入脾胃，脾胃属土，候于肌肉，热盛蕴蒸于外则为发黄，热熏于心胸则为烦躁，津液耗减者则为发渴，热上冲咽喉口舌者则生疮肿疼痛。有血泄者，血得热则流溢妄行，从鼻出者则为衄血，从口出者则吐血，从大便出者则便血，从小便出者则遗血。[24p]

When one suffers from a cold and experiences heat following the cold, if the intense heat has receded but residual heat remains, it indicates excessive treatment of the cold, resulting in a deficiency of the stomach that allows heat to take hold. If there is deficient heat in the stomach, even if it is not much, it is important to generate fluid in the stomach; when fluids are produced, the heat will subside naturally.

When one is attacked by cold and the heat manifests outwardly, it is classified as an exterior condition. If the heat has not penetrated inward, both conditions must be resolved accordingly. If there is internal deficiency and reversed qi, resulting in heat accumulating and hardening in the chest causing pain, this is known as chest constriction; if there is only fullness and hardness without pain, it is known as phlegm qi; if the condition arises after drinking water, it is termed water accumulation.

If the external heat has penetrated inward for three to four days, it can cause abdominal fullness and phlegm if there are dry stools; in such cases, one must induce a bowel movement. If the heat enters the large intestine, it results in constipation with hard stools; if it enters the small intestine, it leads to difficulty in urination; if heat infiltrates both large and small intestines, it results in complete obstruction of both urination and defecation.

When heat enters the spleen and stomach, which are associated with the earth element and are reflected in the muscles, excess heat may manifest externally as jaundice. If the heat consumes the heart and chest area, it may lead to restlessness; if the bodily fluids are depleted, it results in thirst, and if the heat rushes upward affecting the throat and tongue, it causes sores, swelling, and pain.

In cases of blood loss, if blood is heated, it may overflow uncontrollably: if it flows from the nose, it is called nosebleed; if it comes from the mouth, it is termed hematemesis; if it appears in the stool, it is bloody diarrhea; and if it is found in the urine, it is referred to as hematuria.[24p]

若壮热未汗，躁喘鼻鸣，因衄一升数合而热得歇者，病则解矣；若出至二三升者危矣。若热毒积满于内不得时下，致毒乘瘀血，则烦盛发狂。若燠寒昏冒闷乱者，死。若胃有寒气相搏，则呕啘咳逆；若肺有寒相搏，则咳嗽气急；若气怯者传变入阴，则四肢厥逆，面青体冷，下利清谷。并当随证施治。　　钱乙论伤风伤寒，疮疹伤食，壮热昏睡，一皆相似，若仓卒未能辨认之间，但与升麻葛根汤、惺惺散、小柴胡汤，此数药通治甚验。　　《圣惠》论婴孩伤寒，不可用性燥药发汗，燥加脏腑，热极伤心，则厥逆难治。又不可用性热药，热乃助阳，阳极则阴争，四肢汗出如油，手足或冷或热，多致发狂、颠癎、搐搦，为难治。[25p]

If the strong heat has not yet caused sweating, accompanied by restlessness, panting, and nasal wheezing, but there is a rise in blood pressure and the heat subsides, then the illness is resolved; however, if the discharge reaches two or three liters, it is dangerous. If the heat toxin is full within and does not descend in time, leading to toxins overwhelming stagnant blood, then severe agitation and mania will arise. If there is a combination of heat and cold causing confusion and heaviness, it can lead to death. If there is cold in the stomach causing disturbance, it will result in vomiting, belching, and rebellious qi; if there is cold in the lungs, it will lead to coughing and shortness of breath; if the qi is weak and transforms into yin, it will result in cold limbs, a pale face, body coldness, and clear diarrhea. Treatment should be based on the symptoms presented.

Qian Yi discusses colds and fevers, rashes, and eating disorders, which all share similarities. If one cannot discern between them in a rush, administering Shengma Gancao Decoction, Xingsheng Powder, or Xiaochaihu Decoction—a few medicines serve as effective general treatments.

The "Shenghui" also states that in cases of infantile fevers, one must not use excessively drying medicines to induce sweating, as drying can injure the organs. Extreme heat can harm the heart, making reversal difficult. Furthermore, one should not use hot medicines, as heat supports yang; when yang is extreme, yin contends, resulting in profuse sweating like oil from the limbs, which may be alternately cold or hot, often leading to agitation, seizures, and convulsions, making them difficult to treat.[25p]

又不可用性寒药，寒则阳受其冷，则寒热相击，一向叫啼不睡，使热上冲于脑，则头骨缝开为难治。予流落钱塘，就馆于亲豪苏伯正防御家，伯正以医治伤寒名。予常观其用药次第。若小儿伤寒壮热，头痛体疼，脉大鼻塞，声重嚏咳，呵欠恶风憎寒，病在表可汗者，用银白散；热多者甘露散；有食饮宿滞，脾胃不和者，以安胃丸间服；胸膈不快者，以香壳散间服；烦渴饮水，或作寒热者，灵砂散间服；有惊者，天麻防风丸、人参化风膏；涎盛欬嗽者，小珍珠丸。如此施治，随手得愈者，十有八九；余一二者，乃病久传深，或已成变证。方才请召，亦依法调治，乃得痊可。其所用之药，多非古方，性不燥热，率皆温平，是谓晓南北之异地，识寒热之所宜，深通古人治病之大体也。[26p]

One must also avoid using cold remedies, for if the cold affects the yang, the clash of cold and heat will lead to continuous crying and sleeplessness. If heat rises to the head, it can cause the skull sutures to open, making it difficult to treat. I found myself in Qiantang, staying at the home of a relative, Su Bozheng, a well-known practitioner of medicine for treating typhoid fever. I often observed his method of prescribing medication. When a child suffers from typhoid fever with strong heat, symptoms like headache, body aches, a strong pulse, nasal congestion, heavy voice, sneezing, coughing, yawning, aversion to wind, and dislike of cold, and the disease is on the surface leading to sweating, he would use Silver White Powder; if there's excessive heat, Sweet Dew Powder; for issues with food stagnation, where the stomach and spleen are not in harmony, he would use An Wei Pills intermittently; for chest discomfort, he would use Fragrant Shell Powder intermittently; for thirst and the urge to drink, or when alternating between cold and heat, he would use Ling Sha Powder intermittently; if there is fright, he would use Tianma Fangfeng Pills or Ginseng Wind Resolving Ointment; for excessive saliva and coughing, he would use Small Pearl Pills. With this treatment approach, the recovery rate is quite high, about eighty to ninety percent. Only one or two cases are ones where the illness has persisted deeply or has developed into a more severe condition. When called for treatment, if he follows the prescribed methods, recovery can be achieved. Most of the medicines he uses are not from ancient formulas, and they are not excessively warming. Generally, they are mild and balanced, demonstrating a keen understanding of the differences between cold and heat in various regions, as well as a profound comprehension of the ancient principles of disease treatment.[26p]

　　　　活幼精要 【明　董凤翀】

　　　　　伤寒

　　凡治伤寒，须别表里。表里不分，汗下差误。表证当汗，里证当下。发表攻里，不易之法。表证属阳，病在六腑。里证属阴，病在五脏。阳盛阴虚，汗之即死，下之当愈。阳虚阴盛，下之即死，汗之即愈。阳虚外寒，阴虚内热，阳盛外热，阴盛内寒。不汗强汗，津溢枯竭。合汗不汗，窍闷闭绝。不下强下，洞泄不禁。合下不下，肿胀闷乱。犯此数者，皆是死证。古今图书集成医部全录卷四百十八

小儿风寒门

　　　　方

　　五味子汤 【《千金方》，下同】 　治小儿伤寒病久不除，瘥后复剧，瘦瘠骨立。　　五味子十铢　大黄　黄连　黄芩　麦门冬　前胡各六铢　芒硝五铢　石膏一两　甘草　当归各十二铢　　右十味(口父)咀，以水三升，煮取一升半，服二合，得下便止，计大小增减之。[27p]

Essentials for Treating Childhood Illnesses
Ming Dynasty - Dong Fengchong

Febrile Illnesses

In treating febrile illnesses, one must differentiate between exterior and interior conditions. Failure to make this distinction can lead to mistakes in sweating or purging. When the exterior condition is present, sweating is indicated; when the interior condition is present, purging is indicated. Attacking the interior when the exterior condition is present is not an effective method. The exterior conditions belong to Yang and affect the six bowels, while the interior conditions belong to Yin and affect the five organs. When Yang is excessive and Yin is deficient, sweating will lead to death, while purging should lead to recovery. Conversely, when Yang is deficient and Yin is excessive, purging will lead to death, while sweating should lead to recovery.
When Yang is deficient with external cold and Yin is deficient with internal heat, or when Yang is excessive with external heat and Yin is excessive with internal cold, inappropriate sweating will result in fluid overflow and exhaustion. Failure to sweat or excessive sweating will lead to obstruction of the openings and stagnation. Inappropriate purging or excessive purging will cause uncontrolled diarrhea. Failure to purge will lead to swelling and discomfort. Violating any of these principles may result in fatality.

Collection of Ancient and Modern Medical Texts, Volume 418

Pediatric Cold and Flu Formulas

Schisandra Decoction
(To treat long-lasting febrile illness in children that does not resolve, worsening after improvement, and leading to emaciation and skeleton-like appearance):

  • Schisandra berries: 10 grams
  • Rhubarb: 6 grams
  • Coptis: 6 grams
  • Scutellaria: 6 grams
  • Ophiopogon: 6 grams
  • Liquorice: 12 grams
  • Angelica: 12 grams
  • Glauber’s salt: 5 grams
  • Gypsum: 30 grams
  • The above ten ingredients should be crushed and boiled with 3 liters of water until 1.5 liters remain. Take 200 ml; stop further use upon achieving an effect. Adjust dosage based on size and condition.[27p]

　　莽草浴汤　治少小伤寒。
　　莽草半斤　雷丸三十枚　蛇床子炒，一升　牡蛎四两　大黄一两　　右五味，以水三斗，煮取斗半，适寒温以浴儿，避眼及阴。　　又　治小儿卒寒热不佳，不能服药。　　莽草　丹参　桂心各三两　石菖蒲半斤　雷丸一升　蛇床子二两　　右六味，以水二斗，煮三五沸，适寒温以浴儿，避眼及阴。
　　雷丸浴汤　治小儿忽寒热。
　　雷丸二十枚　大黄四两　黄芩一两　苦参　石膏各三两　丹参二两　　右六味(口父)咀，以水二斗，煮取一斗半，浴儿，避眼及阴。浴讫，以粉粉之，勿厚衣。一宿复浴。
　　麦门冬汤　治小儿未满百日，伤寒鼻衄，身热呕逆。　　麦门冬十八铢　石膏　寒水石　甘草各半两　桂心八铢　　右五味(口父)咀，以水二升半，煮取一升，每服一合，日三。[28p]

Mao Grass Bath Decoction treats minor children's cold.

Mao grass half a pound, thirty pieces of thunder pill, one sheng of fried snake bed seed, four taels of oyster, one tael of rhubarb. Combine these five ingredients with three dou of water, boil down to one and a half dou, adjust to a suitable temperature for bathing the child, avoiding the eyes and private parts.

Additionally, to treat a child's sudden cold and fever with poor response and inability to take medicine: Mao grass, salvia miltiorrhiza, and cinnamon heart each three taels, half a pound of stone calamus, one sheng of thunder pill, two taels of snake bed seed. Combine these six ingredients with two dou of water, boil until three to five bubbles, adjust to a suitable temperature for bathing the child, avoiding the eyes and private parts.

Thunder Pill Bath Decoction treats a sudden cold and fever in children.

Twenty pieces of thunder pill, four taels of rhubarb, one tael of huangqin, three taels each of bitter gentian and gypsum, two taels of salvia miltiorrhiza. Combine these six ingredients, chop, with two dou of water, boil down to one and a half dou, bathe the child, avoiding the eyes and private parts. After bathing, dust with powder, do not dress too heavily. Bathe again after one night.

Mai Men Dong Decoction treats children under a hundred days old with cold, nasal bleeding, body heat, and vomiting.

Eighteen zhū of mai men dong, half a tael each of gypsum, cold water stone, and licorice, eight zhū of cinnamon heart. Combine these five ingredients, chop, with two and a half sheng of water, boil down to one sheng, administer one dose three times a day.[28p]

　　芍药四物解肌汤　治少小伤寒。
　　芍药　黄芩　升麻　葛根各半两
　　右四味，以水三升，煮取九合，去滓分服。期岁以上，分三服。
　　麻黄汤　治少小伤寒发热咳嗽，头面热者。　　麻黄　生姜　黄芩各一两　甘草　桂心　石膏　芍药各半两　杏仁十枚　　右八味(口父)咀，以水四升，煮取一升半，分二服；儿若小，以意减之。《古今医统》曰：前方治伤寒头痛发热，腰疼骨节痛，恶寒无汗而喘，以此汗之。盖暖取汗，漐漐至手心足心而止，不须再服。
　　羌活散 【《钱氏直诀》，下同】 　治风邪所伤，头目昏眩，痰涎壅滞，肢节烦疼。　　羌活　前胡　麻黄　白茯苓　川芎　黄芩　炙甘草　蔓荆子　枳壳麸炒　细辛　石膏　菊花　防风各等分　　右为末，每服一二钱，水煎。[29p]

Peony Four Herbs Decoction treats mild and minor cold.
Peony, Huangqin, Shengma, and Gancao, each half a liang.
Take these four ingredients, use three sheng of water, boil down to nine portions, strain, and divide for consumption. For those over a year old, divide into three doses.

Ephedra Decoction treats mild cold with fever and cough, and heat in the head and face.
Ephedra, Shengjiang, Huangqin each one liang; Gancao, Guixin, Shigao, and Peony each half a liang; ten pieces of Xingren.
These eight ingredients should be chewed, use four sheng of water, boil down to one and a half sheng, and divide into two doses; for children, reduce as appropriate. "Ancient and Modern Medical Compendium" states: this prescription treats cold with headache, fever, aching lower back and joints, chills without sweat and wheezing. This should induce sweating, gradually until palms and soles are warm, without needing another dose.

Qianghuo Powder treats wind-evil damage, dizziness of the head, phlegm and fluid congestion, and painful limbs and joints.
Qianghuo, Qianhu, Ephedra, Baifuling, Chuanxiong, Huangqin, roasted Gancao, Muxiang, Zhihua cooked in bran, Xixin, Shigao, Ju Hua, and Fangfeng, all in equal portions.
Grind these into a fine powder, take one or two qian, and decoct in water.[29p]

　　大羌活汤
　　羌活　独活　防己　防风　黄芩　黄连　苍朮　白朮　炙甘草　川芎　细辛各二钱　知母　生地黄各一钱　　右为末，每服一二钱，水煎热服。

　　人参羌活散　治伤寒时气，头疼发热。　　人参　羌活　独活　柴胡　前胡　桔梗　茯苓　枳壳麸炒　川芎　天麻　地骨皮　甘草炒，二分　　右入薄荷三叶水煎。薛己曰：按前方乃解肌发表，化痰利气之剂。然元气虚者，宜用清肺散。
　　秘旨清肺散　治感冒发热，鼻流清涕，或咳嗽吐痰。轻者勿药自愈，重者用此轻和之剂。　　橘红　半夏炮　桔梗炒　川芎藭各五分　白茯　桑皮蜜炙，各七分　炙草　防风各四分　薄荷　白朮　枯黄芩炒，各三分　　右每服二三钱，姜水煎。薛己曰：按前证若风邪退而痰热不止，但健中气则痰自化而病自愈。若专用化痰利气，则中气愈虚，痰热愈甚矣。[30p]

Daqiang Huo Decoction
Qianghuo, Duhuo, Fangji, Fangfeng, Huangqin, Huanglian, Cangzhuru, Baizhu, Zhi Gan Cao, Chuanxiong, and Xixin, each 2 qian. Zhimu and Shengdi Huang, each 1 qian. Grind these into a fine powder. Take 1 to 2 qian each time, decoct in water and consume while hot.

Ren Shen Qiang Huo Powder
Treats cold and flu with symptoms of headache and fever. Ren Shen, Qianghuo, Duhuo, Chaihu, Qianhu, Jiegeng, Fuling, Zhixiao (brittle orange peel), Chuanxiong, Tianma, Digupi, and roasted licorice, each 2 fen. Add 3 leaves of mint and decoct in water. Xue Ji states: The previous formula expels wind and promotes sweating, resolves phlegm, and benefits qi. However, those with weak vital energy should use the Qing Fei Powder.

Secret Formula Qing Fei Powder
Treats cold and fever, with clear nasal discharge, or cough with phlegm. In mild cases, no medication is needed as recovery happens spontaneously; in severe cases, use this gentle harmonizing formula. Ju Hong, Banxia (processed), Jiegeng (roasted), Chuanxiong, and Huai Mu Pi, each 5 fen; Bai Fuling and Sang Pi (honey-coated), each 7 fen; roasted licorice and Fangfeng, each 4 fen; mint, Baizhu, and roasted Huangqin, each 3 fen. Take 2 to 3 qian each time, decoct in ginger water. Xue Ji states: If the wind pathogen recedes but phlegm heat persists, strengthening the middle qi will transform phlegm and achieve recovery. If solely focusing on resolving phlegm and benefiting qi, the middle qi may become more deficient, worsening the phlegm heat.[30p]

　　败毒散　治伤寒时气，寒热咳嗽。
　　人参　茯苓　甘草炒　前胡　川芎　羌活　独活　桔梗　柴胡　枳壳麸炒，各等分　　右为末，每服一二钱，生姜薄荷水煎。薛己曰：按《秘旨》云：小儿虽有感冒伤风，鼻塞流涕，发热咳嗽，以降痰为主，略加微解。凡散利败毒，非幼稚所宜。或冒轻者，不必用药，候一二日自愈。窃谓前证若手足冷或腹胀，脾虚也，用六君子汤加柴胡、升麻；若腹胀或虚喘，肺虚也，用四君子汤加柴胡、升麻。盖肺虚则腠理不密，外邪易感。发表之后，其邪既去，即补脾肺以实其表，庶无变证矣。
　　温胃散 【《育婴家秘》】 　如小儿误服寒凉药过多者，以致脾胃虚弱，胃脘痛，宜服此散主之。　　陈皮　黄芪炙，各七钱　缩砂仁　甘草炙　厚朴姜汁炒　益智仁各四钱　白豆蔻仁　泽泻　干姜炮　姜黄各三钱　人参二钱　共细末，每服五分至一钱，水煎去滓，食前温服。[31p]

Baidusan: For treating cold-induced illnesses, chills and fever, cough.

Ingredients include: Ren Shen (Ginseng), Fu Ling (Poria), stir-fried Gan Cao (Licorice), Qian Hu (Hogfennel), Chuan Xiong (Szechuan Lovage), Qiang Huo (Notopterygium), Du Huo (Angelica Pubescens), Jie Geng (Platycodon), Chai Hu (Bupleurum), Zhi Ke (Bitter Orange) stir-fried, in equal parts. Grind into powder. Take one to two qian (a unit of weight), decoct with ginger and mint water. Xue Ji said: According to the "Secret Instructions," even if a child has a cold with symptoms such as nasal congestion, runny nose, fever, and cough, the main focus is to reduce phlegm with slight relief from the symptoms. Generally, dispersing toxins is not suitable for young children. If symptoms are mild, it may not be necessary to use medicine; wait one to two days for self-recovery. I suggest that if symptoms include cold hands and feet or abdominal distension, indicating spleen deficiency, use Liu Jun Zi Tang (Six Gentlemen Decoction) with added Chai Hu and Sheng Ma; if there is abdominal distension or weak breathing, indicating lung deficiency, use Si Jun Zi Tang (Four Gentlemen Decoction) with added Chai Hu and Sheng Ma. Indeed, if the lungs are deficient, the defensive qi is weak and external pathogens can easily enter. After expelling pathogens, the internal organs should be nourished to strengthen the surface, ensuring no changes in the condition.

Wen Wei San [from "Secrets of Infant Care"]: This is used when a child mistakenly consumes too much cold medicine, resulting in weakness of the spleen and stomach, and abdominal pain.

Ingredients include: Chen Pi (Dried Tangerine Peel), Huang Qi (Astragalus) stir-fried, each seven qian; Suo Shan Ren (Amomum Fruit), Gan Cao (Licorice) stir-fried, Hou Po (Magnolia Bark) with ginger juice stir-fried, Yi Zhi Ren (Alpinia) each four qian; Bai Dou Kou (White Cardamom), Ze Xie (Alisma), Gan Jiang (Dried Ginger) processed, Jiang Huang (Turmeric) each three qian; Ren Shen (Ginseng) two qian, all ground into fine powder. Take five fen (a smaller unit of weight) to one qian, decoct with water, filter out the dregs, and take warm before meals.[31p]

　　洗心散 【《类证活人书》，下同】 　治遍身壮热，头目碎痛，背髆拘急，大热冲上，口苦唇焦，夜卧舌干，咽喉肿痛，涕唾稠粘，痰壅，吃食不进，心神躁热，眼濇睛疼，伤寒鼻塞，四肢沉重，语声不出，百骨节痛，大小便不利，麸豆疮，时行温疫，狂语多渴，及小儿天吊风，夜惊，并宜服之。　　当归四两，炒　芍药四两，生用　甘草四两，炙　荆芥四两　白朮一两，炒　麻黄四两，去节炒　大黄四两，以米泔水浸一炊间，漉出令干慢炒　　右捣罗为细末，每服抄二钱，水一盏，入姜一片，薄荷二叶，同煎至八分，放温和滓服了，仰卧，仍去枕少时。如五脏壅实，煎四五钱匕；若要溏转则热服。[32p]

Washing the Heart and Scattering

For the treatment of pervasive body heat, headaches, back pain and stiffness, intense heat rising, bitter mouth and dry lips, dry tongue at night, swollen and painful throat, thick nasal discharge, phlegm blockage, loss of appetite, restless heart and mind, dry eyes and eye pain, chills and stuffy nose due to cold damage, heavy limbs, inability to speak, pain in bones and joints, difficulty in urination and defecation, skin eruptions, intermittent febrile epidemics, excessive thirst and talking nonsense, as well as conditions in children such as the rapture of heaven and night terrors, one should also take this.

Ingredients: 4 taels of cooked Angelica, 4 taels of raw Peony, 4 taels of licorice, 4 taels of fried Schizonepeta, 1 tael of Atractylodes, 4 taels of fried Ephedra (remove the nodes), 4 taels of fried Rhubarb (soaked in rice wash for a short period, then dried and lightly fried). Grind the above into a fine powder. Each dose is 2 qian (a measure), mixed with a bowl of water, add a slice of ginger and two leaves of mint. Boil until reduced to about 80%, let cool, and drink the residue while lying on your back without a pillow for a short time. If the five organs are congested, use about 4 to 5 qian; if a loose stool is desired, take it hot.[32p]

　　惺惺散　治小儿风热及伤寒时气，疮疹发热。　　桔梗　细辛　人参　白朮　瓜蒌根　甘草炙　白茯苓　川芎各等分　　右捣罗为末，每服二钱，用水一盏，生姜二片，薄荷二叶，同煎七分服。三岁已下作四五服，五岁已上分二服。凡小儿发热，不问伤风风热，先与此散，数服往往辄愈。[33p]

Xingxing San is used to treat children's wind-heat and seasonal febrile illnesses, as well as fevers due to sores and rashes. The ingredients are as follows: Platycodon grandiflorum, Asarum, Ginseng, Atractylodes macrocephala, Trichosanthes root, roasted Licorice, Bai Fu Ling, and Chuanxiong, all in equal parts.

Grind the above ingredients into a powder. For each dose, take two qian, mix with one bowl of water, add two slices of fresh ginger and two leaves of mint, and decoct until reduced to seven portions. For children up to three years old, administer four to five doses, and for those five years and older, divide into two doses.

In cases of fever in children, regardless of whether it’s due to a cold or wind-heat, this powder is often effective when given several times, leading to recovery.[33p]

　　麻黄黄芩汤　小儿伤寒无汗，头疼发热恶寒。　　麻黄去节，一两　黄芩炒　赤芍药各半两　甘草炙　桂枝去皮，各一分　　右捣罗为细末，每服二钱，滚水调下，日三服。兼治天行热气，生豌豆疮不快，益烦躁昏愦，或出尚身疼热者。
　　升麻黄芩汤　治小儿伤风有汗，头痛发热恶寒。　　升麻　葛根　黄芩　芍药各三钱　炙草一钱半　　右銼如麻豆大，每服二钱，以水一中盏，煎至六分，去滓温服。若时行疮痘出不快，烦躁不眠者，加木香一钱五分。
　　甘露饮子　治胃中客热口臭，不思饮食，或饥烦不欲食，齿龈肿疼，脓血，口舌咽中有疮，赤眼赤脸，目不欲开，疮疹已发未发，并宜服之。　　熟地黄　生地黄　天门冬　麦门冬并去心焙　枇杷叶去毛　枳壳麸炒　黄芩　石斛去苗　山茵陈　甘草炙，各等分　　右为细末，每服二钱，水一盏，煎至六分，食后临卧，去滓温服。[34p]

Mahuang Huangqin Decoction: For children with typhoid fever, no sweating, headache, fever, and aversion to cold.

Shengma Huangqin Decoction: For children with wind-cold and sweating, headache, fever, and aversion to cold.

Ganlu Drink: For heat in the stomach leading to foul breath, loss of appetite, or hunger with no desire to eat, swollen and painful gums, pus and blood, sores in the mouth, throat, red eyes and face, and difficulty opening eyes, whether rashes have appeared or not.
