　　双丸　治小儿身热头痛，饮食不消，腹胀满，或心腹疼痛，大小便不利，或下重数起，未瘥可再服。小儿蒸候，哺食减少，气息不快，夜啼不眠，是腹内不调，并宜用此丸下之。　　甘遂半两　朱砂一钱，另研　麦冬二两半，去心　蕤核去仁，四两半　牡蛎二两，煅　甘草一两，炙　巴豆六十枚，去皮心膜研，新布绞去油，日中晒之白如霜者　　右麦门冬、甘草、甘遂、牡蛎四味为细末，入巴豆、朱砂、蕤仁合和捣二千杵，更入少蜜捣和极熟，旋丸。半岁儿服如荏子大一双；一岁儿服如半麻子大，分为一双服；如二岁麻子大一枚，分一双；三四岁者服如麻子大二丸；五六岁者服如大麻子大二丸；七八岁者如小豆大二丸；十岁微大于小豆二丸。常以鸡鸣时服。如至日出时不下者，热粥饮服数合，投之即下，药丸皆双出也。下利甚者，浓煎冷粥饮之便止。[35p]

Shuang Wan: Treats children's fever, headaches, poor digestion, abdominal bloating, or pain in the heart and abdomen, difficulty with urination and defecation, or frequent urges without relief. If the condition has not improved, it can be taken again. For children with steaminess, reduced food intake, poor breathing, and night crying with sleeplessness, this pill may also help with internal imbalances.

Ingredients:

  • Half a tael of Gan Sui
  • One qian of Zhusha, separately ground
  • Two and a half taels of Mai Dong, heart removed
  • Four and a half taels of Ruo He, kernel removed
  • Two taels of Mu Li, calcined
  • One tael of Gan Cao, roasted
  • Sixty pieces of Ba Dou, skin and heart membranes removed, ground, then wrapped in new cloth to squeeze out oil, dried in the sun until white as frost.

Preparation: Grind the aforementioned Mai Dong, Gan Cao, Gan Sui, and Mu Li into a fine powder, then combine with Ba Dou, Zhusha, and Ruo Ren, and pound together vigorously until well mixed. Add a small amount of honey and pound until thoroughly blended, then form into pills.

Dosage:

  • For a six-month-old, take one pill the size of a sesame seed;
  • For one year old, take half the size of a sesame seed, divided into two doses;
  • For a two-year-old, take one pill the size of a sesame seed, divided into two;
  • For ages three to four, take two pills the size of sesame seeds;
  • For ages five to six, take two pills the size of large sesame seeds;
  • For ages seven to eight, take two pills the size of small beans;
  • For ten-year-olds, take two pills slightly larger than small beans.

Administer at crowing rooster time. If symptoms persist until sunrise, consume hot porridge or drink several doses to encourage bowel movements; all pills should be expelled. If diarrhea is severe, drink a strong decoction of cold porridge to stop it.[35p]

　　石膏麻桂汤　治小儿伤寒未发热，咳漱头面赤。　　黄芩　麻黄一两，去节汤泡　甘草炙　石膏　芍药各半两　桂心一分　杏仁十枚，去皮尖　　右七味为散，每服二钱，水一中盏，入生姜二片，煎半盏，去滓服。儿若甚小，以意增减之。
　　连翘饮　治小儿一切热。
　　连翘　防风　甘草　山栀子各等分
　　右件捣罗为末，每服二钱，水一中盏，煎七分，温服。
　　十物升麻汤　治小儿伤寒变热毒病，身热面赤，口燥，心腹坚急，大小便不利，或口疮，或因壮热便四肢挛掣惊，仍作癎疾，时发时醒，醒后身热如火者。　　升麻　白薇　麻黄去根节　萎蕤　柴胡　甘草各半两，炙　黄芩一两　(石卜)硝　大黄　钓滕各一分　　右銼如麻豆大，每服三钱，水一盏，煎至七分，去滓下硝，再煎化温服。[36p]

Gypsochalcum and Cinnamon Decoction: For treating children with cold that has not yet developed a fever, presenting with a cough and a flushed face.

Ingredients:

  • 1 liang (approx. 37.5g) Huangqin (Scutellaria)
  • 1 liang Ma Huang (Ephedra), remove joints and soak in decoction
  • 0.5 liang Licorice (Gancao), roasted
  • 0.5 liang Gypsochalcum (Shigao)
  • 0.5 liang Shaoyao (Paeonia)
  • 0.1 liang Gui Xin (Cinnamon heart)
  • 10 pieces of Apricot kernel, peeled and pointed

Preparation: The seven ingredients above are ground into a powder. Each dose is 2 qian (approx. 6g), boiled with 1 medium cup of water, adding two slices of fresh ginger, decoct until reduced to half a cup, and discard the residue. Adjust dosage if the child is very small.

Forsythia Drink: For treating all types of fever in children.

Ingredients:

  • Equal parts of Lianqiao (Forsythia), Fangfeng (Saposhnikovia), Gancao (Licorice), and Shan Zhi Zi (Gardenia).

Preparation: Grind the ingredients into a powder. Each dose is 2 qian (approx. 6g), boiled with 1 medium cup of water until reduced to seven parts, taken warm.

Ten Ingredient Sheng Ma Decoction: For treating children with cold that has transformed into a febrile toxic illness, with body heat, a flushed face, dry mouth, a tense and hard abdomen, difficulty in urination and defecation, or oral sores. It may also cause severe heat, resulting in limb convulsions and seizures, where the child alternates between consciousness and unconsciousness, feeling feverish upon waking.

Ingredients:

  • 0.5 liang Sheng Ma (Cimicifuga)
  • 0.5 liang Bai Wei (Cynanchum)
  • 1 liang Ma Huang (Ephedra), root and joints removed
  • 0.5 liang Wei Rui (Hesperidin)
  • 0.5 liang Chai Hu (Bupleurum)
  • 0.5 liang Gancao (Licorice), roasted
  • 1 liang Huangqin (Scutellaria)
  • 0.1 liang (Stone) Xie (Natrii Sulfas)
  • 0.1 liang Da Huang (Rhubarb)
  • 0.1 liang Diao Teng (Lathyrus)

Preparation: Grind the above to a size of a large soybean. Each dose is 3 qian (approx. 9g), boiled with 1 cup of water until reduced to seven parts, discard the residue, add the natrii sulfas, and decoct until dissolved, then taken warm.[36p]

　　六物黄芩汤　治少小腹大短气，热有进退，食不安，谷为之不化。　　黄芩　大青　甘草炙　麦门冬　石膏各半两　桂心三钱　　右銼如麻豆大，每服三钱，水一盏，煎七分，温服。
　　五物人参饮　治小儿天行壮热，咳嗽，心腹胀满。　　人参　甘草各半两，炙　麦门冬一两，去心　生地黄一两半，如无只用干生地半两　　右銼如麻豆大，每服三钱，水一盏，入茅根半握，煎至七分，去滓温服。
　　八物麦门冬饮　治证同前。
　　麦门冬三两，去心　甘草炙　人参各一分　紫苑　升麻各二两　贝母一分半　　右銼如麻豆大，每服三钱，水一盏，入茅根半握，煎至七分，去滓再入竹沥少许，重煎服。[37p]

Liu Wu Huangqin Decoction: This treats lower abdominal distension and shortness of breath, with alternating heat symptoms, discomfort after eating, and indigestion. Ingredients: Huangqin, Daqing, roasted Licorice, Maidong, and gypsum, each 250 grams; Guixin 9 grams. Prepare by grinding to the size of a soybean, take 9 grams each time with one cup of water, simmer to 70% remaining, and take warm.

Wu Wu Ren Shen Drink: This treats children with seasonal fevers, cough, and abdominal distension. Ingredients: Ren Shen and Licorice, each 250 grams, roasted; Maidong 500 grams, remove the heart; Sheng Dihuang 750 grams; if unavailable, use 375 grams of dry Sheng Dihuang. Prepare by grinding to the size of a soybean, take 9 grams each time with one cup of water, add half a handful of reed root, simmer to 70% remaining, strain, and take warm.

Ba Wu Maidong Drink: This treats the same symptoms as above. Ingredients: Maidong 450 grams, remove the heart; roasted Licorice 3 grams; Ren Shen 3 grams; Ziyuan and Shengma 600 grams each; Beimu 4.5 grams. Prepare by grinding to the size of a soybean, take 9 grams each time with one cup of water, add half a handful of reed root, simmer to 70% remaining, strain, then add a little bamboo juice, re-simmer, and take.[37p]

　　枣叶饮　治小儿天行五日以后，热不歇者。　　枣叶半握　麻黄半两，去根节　淡豆豉一合　葱白切，一合　　右件共童子小便二盏，煎至一盏，去滓分二服。
　　羌活散 【《婴童百问》，下同】 　治风寒惊热。　　羌活　独活　前胡　柴胡　川芎　白茯苓　桔梗　枳壳　人参　地骨皮　天麻各等分　生甘草减半　　右銼散，生姜薄荷煎。加麻黄、干葛，薏苡仁，治中风体硬。加蝉蜕，治惊热。
　　柴胡散　治小儿伤寒无汗有表证，壮热头疼，身体痛，口干烦渴，小便赤，大便秘濇，夹惊腮肿。　　石膏　黄芩　甘草　赤芍药　葛根各二钱半　麻黄去节　柴胡各半两　　右銼散，三岁儿每服二钱，水一盏，生姜少许，葱白三寸，豆豉一撮，煎至七分，不拘时温服。
　　三黄散　解伤风热证。
　　白朮　大黄蒸　赤芍药半两　黄芩三钱　麻黄去节，一钱　桂枝二钱　　右(口父)咀，生姜一片，枣二枚，水一盏，煎七分，温服。[38p]

Jujube Leaf Decoction: For treating children after five days of a seasonal fever with persistent heat. Take half a handful of jujube leaves, half a tael of ephedra (root and joints removed), one portion of plain fermented soybean, and one portion of scallion whites chopped. Combine these with two cups of the child's urine and boil down to one cup, then strain and divide into two doses.

Qianghuo Powder: For treating cold-induced shock fever. Equal parts of: qianghuo, duhuo, fangfeng, chaihu, chuanxiong, baizhu, jiegeng, zhuke, ginseng, digupi, tianma. Use half the amount of raw licorice. Grind into powder, decoct with ginger and mint. Add ephedra and dried kudzu, and coix seeds for treating stiffness from stroke. Add cicada slough for treating shock fever.

Chaihu Powder: For treating children with typhoid fever without sweating, presenting with exterior symptoms, high fever, headache, body aches, dry mouth, thirst, red urine, and constipation, along with signs of shock and swollen cheeks. Use two and a half qian of gypsum, huangqin, licorice, and red peony, and two and a half qian of kudzu, half a tael of ephedra (joints removed) and chaihu. Grind into powder; for a three-year-old, each dose is two qian, with one cup of water, a little ginger, three inches of scallion, and a pinch of fermented soybean, decoct until reduced by 30%, taken warm at any time.

Three Huang Powder: For alleviating symptoms of wind-heat. Ingredients include: baizhu, steamed dahuang, half a tael of red peony, three qian of huangqin, one qian of ephedra (joints removed), and two qian of cinnamon twig. Grind and combine with one slice of ginger, two jujubes, and one cup of water, decoct to reduce by 30%, taken warm.[38p]

　　抱龙丸　治伤风温疫，身热气粗，痰实壅嗽，常服安神镇惊；亦治疹痘壮热。小儿宜时与服。　　胆星一两　天竺黄　雄黄　辰砂各二钱　麝香少许　　右为末，煮甘草汁丸樱桃大，阴干薄荷汤吞下。气喘有痰，加杏仁。
　　竹叶石膏汤　治伤寒表里俱虚，遍身胸烦闷，或得汗已解，内无津液，虚羸少气，气逆欲吐，及诸虚烦伤寒解后；伤寒未解，切不可服。　　石膏四两　半夏六钱　人参　甘草各半两　麦门冬去心一两　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，生姜一片，粳米五十粒，煎米熟为度，去滓温服。呕者加生姜三片，竹叶数片。
　　辰砂七宝散　治小儿壮热，伤风壅热；冶夹惊伤寒，解诸般热；亦治疹痘热；治惊风，定搐搦。　　麻黄去节　白朮炒　当归酒洗　赤芍药　生大黄　荆芥穗　前胡去芦　生地黄酒洗　生甘草各半两　　右为末，每服三钱。伤风发散，用生薄荷泡汤下。急惊加辰砂，薄荷调下。[39p]

Baolong Pill: Treats wind-cold and warm epidemics, with symptoms of body heat, coarse qi, and phlegm obstructing cough. Regular use calms the spirit and settles agitation; also treats fever from rashes and pox. Suitable for children to take periodically.

Ingredients:

  • 1 tael of gallbladder star
  • 2 qians each of Tianzhu yellow, realgar, and cinnabar
  • A small amount of musk

Grind these into a powder, mix with licorice juice to form pills the size of cherries. Dry in the shade and swallow with mint tea. For wheezing with phlegm, add almonds.

Bamboo Leaf Gypsum Decoction: Treats both exterior and interior deficiency from cold damage, with symptoms of overall chest discomfort. If sweating has occurred but there is no internal fluid, symptoms include weakness, shortness of breath, and reverse qi with a desire to vomit, as well as various complications after warmth-induced cold. Do not take if the cold has not been resolved.

Ingredients:

  • 4 taels of gypsum
  • 6 qians of pinellia
  • ½ tael each of ginseng and licorice
  • 1 tael of Ophiopogon (with heart removed)

Macerate these, take 3 qians each time, with a slice of fresh ginger and 50 grains of japonica rice, boiling until rice is cooked, then remove residue and take warm. For vomiting, add 3 slices of ginger and a few bamboo leaves.

Cinnabar Seven Treasures Powder: Treats high fever in children, wind-cold obstructing heat; alleviates shock from cold and resolves various types of heat; also treats fever from rashes and pox; helps calm shock and spasms.

Ingredients:

  • Ephedra (without joints)
  • Fried Atractylodes
  • Angelica (washed with wine)
  • Red peony
  • Fresh rhubarb
  • Schizonepeta spikes
  • Xiangfu (without the reed)
  • Fresh Rehmannia (washed with wine)
  • Fresh licorice (½ tael each)

Grind these into a powder, taking 3 qians each time. For dispersing wind-cold, use fresh mint steeped in water. For urgent shock, add cinnabar and mint to the mixture.[39p]

　　薄荷散　治乳下婴儿鼻塞不通，及治夹惊伤寒，变蒸热。　　薄荷叶半两　羌活　僵蚕炒　白附子　全蝎　生甘草各一钱半　麻黄去节　天竺黄各一钱　　右为末，每服三钱，薄荷汤下。热极生风，加竹沥少许与服。一方，有柴胡、台芎、桔梗、茯苓，无全蝎、僵蚕、天竺黄、白附子。
　　红绵散　治伤风，咳嗽鼻塞，或流清涕。　　全蝎五个，去毒　麻黄去节　僵蚕炒　白芷　川芎　天麻各二钱　生甘草　苏木各一钱　　右銼，绵少许煎服。有热加荆芥。一方有大黄。
　　葱白汤　治头痛不止，身疼渴发热，小便赤黄，脉浮数无汗。　　葛根　芍药　知母各半两　川芎一两　　右(口父)咀，每服二钱，水一小盏，生姜二片，葱白三枚，煎至七分，去滓热服，出汗。如有汗温服，加甘草。治小儿夹惊伤风，并治发疟头疼。呕者加半夏半两。
　　羌活汤　解利邪气伤风。
　　羌活　人参　防风　川芎各一钱[40p]

Peppermint Powder - Treats nasal congestion in infants and addresses combinations of fright, cold, and fever.

  • Ingredients: 15 grams of peppermint leaves, 15 grams of Qiang Huo, 15 grams of fried silkworms, 15 grams of Bai Fu Zi, 15 grams of whole scorpion, 15 grams of raw licorice, 10 grams of Ma Huang (without joints), 10 grams of Tian Zhu Huang.
  • Instructions: Grind the above into a fine powder. Take 9 grams each time, mixed with peppermint decoction. If there is extreme heat with wind, add a little bamboo juice. An alternative includes Chai Hu, Tai Chong, Jie Geng, and Fu Ling, omitting whole scorpion, silkworm, Tian Zhu Huang, and Bai Fu Zi.

Red Cotton Powder - Treats colds, cough, nasal congestion, or clear nasal discharge.

  • Ingredients: 5 whole scorpions (detoxified), Ma Huang (without joints), fried silkworms, 20 grams of Bai Zhi, 20 grams of Chuan Xiong, 20 grams of Tian Ma, 10 grams of raw licorice, 10 grams of Su Mu.
  • Instructions: Grind and decoct with a little cotton until effective. If there is heat, add Jing Jie. One variation includes Da Huang.

Scallion White Soup - Treats persistent headaches, body aches, thirst, fever, dark yellow urine, and a floating rapid pulse without sweating.

  • Ingredients: 30 grams of Ge Gen, 30 grams of Shao Yao, 30 grams of Zhi Mu, 60 grams of Chuan Xiong.
  • Instructions: Chew and prepare with 20 mL of water, 2 slices of ginger, and 3 pieces of scallion whites, decoct until 70% done, then strain and drink warm to induce sweating. If sweating occurs, take warm with added licorice. Also treats children with fright-induced colds and malarial headaches. For vomiting, add 15 grams of Ban Xia.

Qiang Huo Soup - Disperses harmful qi and treats colds.

  • Ingredients: 10 grams each of Qiang Huo, Ren Shen, Fang Feng, and Chuan Xiong.[40p]

　　右銼一剂，生姜三片，薄荷七叶，水一盏，煎至七分，不拘时服。一方，加芍药、甘草。
　　升麻汤　治小儿时行温疫，头痛发热，肢体烦疼，及疮疹已发未发疑似之间；治伤寒中风，憎寒壮热，肢体痛疼，鼻干不得睡；兼治寒暄不时，人多疾疫，乍暖脱着及暑热之忽变阴寒，身体疼痛头重如石者。亦可加柴胡。　　升麻　葛根　白芍药　甘草炙，各一钱　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，水一盏，煎至六分，去滓温服。疮疹亦准此服药，身凉止药。加紫苏、茯苓、川芎，名升麻苏叶散。有热加黄芩。无汗加麻黄。咽喉痛加桔梗。发丹，加黑参，效。
　　解肌汤　治伤寒温病，时行寒疫，头疼项强，畏寒，肢体拘急，骨节烦疼，腰脊强痛，胸膈烦闷，无汗，恶风壮热。　　葛根一两　麻黄去节　芍药　甘草各半两　桂枝二钱半　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，水一盏，枣一枚，煎至六分，去滓稍热服，以汗出为度。一方无桂枝。夏月加石膏、知母各一钱。[41p]

Here is the translated text:

A remedy consists of one dose, three slices of fresh ginger, seven leaves of mint, and one cup of water, boiled down to seven-tenths; take as needed. In another formulation, add peony and licorice.

Shengma Decoction treats children’s seasonal warm epidemics, headaches, fever, pain in the limbs, and rashes that have appeared or are suspected to appear; it also treats cold-induced febrile diseases, aversion to cold, high fever, pain in the limbs, dry nose with inability to sleep; it conservatively addresses cold and flu that appears unexpectedly with an onset of warmth, sudden transitions from heat to cold, accompanied by body aches and a heavy head. Chaihu may also be added.

Ingredients: Shengma, kudzu, white peony, and licorice, each one qian. The above should be ground; each dose is three qian, combined with one cup of water, boiled to six-tenths, strained while hot. For rashes, take the same medicine, and if the body cools, stop taking it. Add perilla, poria, and chuanxiong, known as Shengma Suye Powder. If there's heat, add huangqin. If no sweat, add mahwang. For sore throat, add jiegeng. If there is a rash, add black ginseng for effect.

Jieji Decoction treats cold-induced febrile diseases, seasonal cold epidemics, severe headaches, stiff neck, fear of cold, tightness in the limbs, painful bones and joints, severe waist and spine pain, chest tightness and discomfort, absence of sweat, and aversion to wind and strong heat.

Ingredients: One liang of kudzu, mahuang without joints, half a liang each of peony and licorice, and two and a half qian of cinnamon twig. The above should be ground; each dose is three qian, combined with one cup of water, one date, boiled to six-tenths, strained and taken slightly warm, with the goal of inducing sweat. In another formulation, omit the cinnamon twig. In summer, add one qian each of gypsum andzhi mu.[41p]

　　调中汤　治夏末秋初忽有暴寒，折于盛暑，热结于四肢则壮热头疼，寒伤于胃则下利或血或赤或白，壮热迷闷脉数，宜下之。　　大黄七钱半　桔梗炒　槁本　茯苓　甘草　干葛　黄芩　芍药　白朮各半两　　右(口父)咀，白水煎，量大小加减服。得快气利壮热便歇，去大黄，加黄连、枳壳，止利尤妙；或加地榆，或加当归皆可。感风加荆芥。秋宜下，当下大黄。
　　射干汤　治初秋夏月暴雨冷及天行暴寒，其热喜伏于内，咳嗽曲折不可得气息，喉哑失声，干嗽无睡，喉中如梗[梗　原作「硬」，据文义改。]。　　半夏汤泡，五钱　生姜泡，四钱　射干　杏仁　甘草炙　紫苑　肉桂　枳实炒　当归　橘皮　独活　麻黄去节汤泡，各二钱　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，水二盏，煎至六分，去滓温服。[42p]

Tiaozhong Decoction: This treats a sudden cold at the end of summer and beginning of autumn, a condition caused by an abrupt chill after excessive heat. If it leads to intense heat and headaches in the limbs, or if cold damages the stomach resulting in diarrhea (which may be bloody, red, or white), accompanied by a strong heat sensation and a rapid pulse, it is necessary to purge.

Ingredients:

  • Dahuang (Rhubarb) 7.5 qian
  • Jiegeng (Platycodon) stir-fried
  • Gaoben (Angelica)
  • Fuling (Poria)
  • Gancao (Licorice)
  • Gange (Dried Kudzu)
  • Huangqin (Scutellaria)
  • Shaoyao (Peony)
  • Baizhu (Atractylodes) each 0.5 liang

Crush the above ingredients and decoct with water, adjusting the dosage according to size. If it relieves the oppressive heat, you can stop. If Dahuang is still in it, add Huanglian (Coptis) and Zhishi (Citri Fructus) to stop diarrhea, which is especially effective. Alternatively, you may also add Diyi (Sanguisorba) or Danggui (Angelica) as needed. For wind invasion, add Jingjie (Schizonepeta). It is suitable to use Dahuang when treating this condition.

Shegan Decoction: This treats the sudden cold of early autumn due to violent rain and extreme chill. The heat tends to remain hidden within, causing a cough that is wheezy and makes breathing difficult, leading to hoarseness, loss of voice, a dry cough with sleeplessness, and a sensation of a lump in the throat.

Ingredients:

  • Banxia (Pinellia) decocted for soaking 5 qian
  • Shengjiang (Fresh ginger) soaked 4 qian
  • Shegan (Belamcanda)
  • Xingren (Apricot kernel)
  • Gancao (Licorice) roasted
  • Ziyuan (Aster)
  • Rougui (Cinnamon)
  • Zhishi (Citri Fructus) stir-fried
  • Danggui (Angelica)
  • Jupi (Tangerine peel)
  • Duhuo (Angelica pubescens)
  • Mahuang (Ephedra) without joints, soaked

Each ingredient: 2 qian. Crush and take 3 qian of the mixture, adding to 2 sheng of water. Boil until reduced to 6 portions, then strain and take warm.[42p]

　　半夏桂甘汤　治伏气之病，谓非时有暴寒中人，伏于少阴经，始不觉病，旬月乃发，脉便微弱，咽痛似伤寒，非喉痹之病，次必下利，始用半夏桂甘汤主之，次用四逆散。此病一二日便瘥，古方谓之肾伤寒。　　半夏洗　桂心　甘草炙，各二两
　　右銼如麻豆大，每服三钱，水一盏，煎至六分，放冷，少含细咽之。入生姜三片煎。
　　五苓散　治伤寒温热病，表里未解，头疼发热，口燥咽干，烦渴饮水，或水入即吐，或小便不利，及汗出表解，烦渴不止；又冶霍乱吐利，燥渴引饮。　　泽泻二两半　猪苓　白朮　茯苓各一两半　肉桂一两　　右为细末，每服二钱，热汤调下，不拘时，服讫多饮热汤，有汗出即愈。又治瘀热在里，身发黄痘，浓煎茵陈汤下，食前服。疸病发渴及中暑引饮，亦可用水调服。小儿加白朮末少许。如发虚，加绵黄芪、人参末少许。[43p]

Banha Xiaoguitang treats diseases caused by hidden heat, especially when one is unexpectedly exposed to severe cold. It resides in the Shaoyin meridian, and symptoms may not manifest until several months later, exhibiting weak pulses and throat pain resembling a cold, but not characterized by throat obstruction. There may subsequently be diarrhea. Begin treatment with Banha Xiaoguitang, followed by Sini San. This condition may improve in one or two days; the ancient formula refers to it as kidney cold damage.

Ingredients: Banxia, Guixin, and roasted Gan Cao, each two liang.
Preparation: Grind to the size of a soybean, take three qian with one cup of water, and simmer until down to six parts. Allow to cool and sip slowly. Add three slices of fresh ginger for boiling.

Wuling San treats febrile diseases due to invasion of cold or heat, where symptoms such as headaches, fever, dry mouth and throat, and intense thirst arise. Patients may experience nausea, vomiting, or difficulty urinating, alongside sweating that does not alleviate thirst. It also addresses cholera with vomiting and diarrhea, and unrelenting thirst necessitating drinking water.

Ingredients: Zexie two and a half liang, Zhuling, Baizhu, and Fuling each one and a half liang, with Rouwu one liang.
Preparation: Grind into fine powder, take two qian with hot soup at any time. After taking, drink plenty of hot soup until sweating occurs to promote recovery. It also treats interior heat causing yellowish skin eruptions; one can ingest a concentrated infusion of Yinchentang before meals. For jaundice with thirst or heatstroke leading to intense thirst, it can also be mixed with water for consumption. For children, add a small amount of Baizhu powder. If experiencing fatigue, add a little cotton Huangqi or Ginseng powder.[43p]

　　萎蕤汤　治风温冬温，及春月中风伤寒，发热头疼，咽干舌强，胸腹满，腰脊强。　　萎蕤三钱　石膏一两　白薇　葛根　羌活　麻黄　川芎　杏仁去皮尖　炙草　木香各半两　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，水一盏，煎至八分，去滓温服。
　　七宝散　治时气头昏体热，此药大人可服，小儿乳母服。　　紫苏　香附炒，各三两　陈皮　甘草炙　桔梗　白芷　川芎各一两　　右(口父)咀，每服二钱，水半盏，姜一片，枣一枚，煎三分，去滓服。有热，加葛根、升麻、荆芥。
　　柴胡石膏汤　治时行瘟疫，壮热恶风，头痛体疼，鼻塞咽干，心胸烦满，寒热往来，痰热咳嗽，涕唾稠粘并疗之。　　黄芩三两　升麻二两半　石膏　前胡　赤芍　干葛　柴胡各五两　荆芥穗　桑白皮各三两　　右为粗末，每服二钱，水一盏，生姜二片，淡豉十粒，煎至七分，去滓稍热服。小儿分作三服，量大小加减，不拘时候。无汗，加麻黄、半夏、北五味。[44p]

Wei Rui Decoction: Treats wind-heat during winter and spring with symptoms of fever, headache, dry throat, stiff tongue, chest and abdomen fullness, and stiffness in the waist and spine.
Ingredients: 3 qian of Wei Rui, 1 liang of Gypsum, 0.5 liang each of Bai Wei, Ge Gen, Qiang Huo, Ma Huang, Chuan Xiong, peeled and pointed apricot kernel, honey-fried licorice, and Mu Xiang.
Preparation: Grind the ingredients finely. Take 3 qian (9 grams) with 1 cup of water, decoct until reduced to 80%, strain, and take warm.

Seven Treasures Powder: Treats dizziness and body heat from seasonal influences; this medicine can be taken by adults and nursing mothers.
Ingredients: 3 liang of Zi Su and Xiang Fu (stir-fried), and 1 liang each of Chen Pi, honey-fried licorice, Jie Geng, Bai Zhi, and Chuan Xiong.
Preparation: Grind the ingredients finely. Take 2 qian (6 grams) with half a cup of water, add 1 slice of ginger and 1 date, decoct to reduce by one-third, strain, and take. If there is heat, add Ge Gen, Sheng Ma, and Jing Jie.

Chai Hu and Gypsum Decoction: Treats epidemic diseases with severe fever and aversion to wind, headache, body pain, nasal congestion, dry throat, agitation in the chest, alternating chills and fever, phlegm heat cough, and thick sputum.
Ingredients: 3 liang of Huang Qin, 2.5 liang of Sheng Ma, and 5 liang each of Shi Gao, Qian Hu, Chi Shao, Gan Ge, and Chai Hu; 3 liang each of Jing Jie spikes and mulberry white bark.
Preparation: Grind to a coarse powder. Take 2 qian (6 grams) with 1 cup of water, add 2 slices of fresh ginger and 10 pieces of light fermented soybeans, decoct until reduced to 70%, strain, and take warm. For children, divide into three doses, adjusting based on size. If there is no sweating, add Ma Huang, Ban Xia, and Bei Wu Wei.[44p]

　　葛根汤　治太阳病项强兀兀，恶风无汗，不恶寒，刚痓。　　葛根四两　麻黄　肉桂各一两　生甘草　芍药各二两　　右銼，每服五钱，水一盏半，入生姜五片，枣二枚，煎七分，去滓服，取微汗为度。

Ge Gen Decoction: Treats Taiyang disease with stiff neck, aversion to wind with no sweat, and no aversion to cold, with rigidity. Gui Zhi and Ma Huang Half Decoction: Treats Taiyang disease after 8 to 9 days, appearing like malaria, with fever and aversion to cold, more heat than cold; if the person does not vomit, has clear stools, and desires to eat, with pulse weak and slow, they are likely to recover; if pulse is weak with aversion to cold, this means yin and yang are not rising, requiring further sweating and purging; if face is red, they are not ready to resolve as they cannot achieve slight sweating and skin will itch. Ingredients: 8 qian of Gui Zhi, and ½ tael each of Shao Yao, Sheng Jiang, Gan Cao, and Ma Huang, 14 peeled apricot kernels, and 2 jujubes. 　　小承气汤　冶太阳病，吐下后发汗而微烦，小便数，大便坚，宜。阳明病，若汗出多而微恶寒，为外未解，无潮热，不可与之；若腹满不大便，可少少与之。　　大黄微炒　枳实炒，各一两　厚朴制，半两　　右(口父)咀，煎。阳明病潮热，大便微硬，可与大承气汤，不硬者不可与之。若不便六七日，恐有燥屎。欲知之法，少与小承气汤，腹中转失气者，此有燥屎也，乃可攻之；若不转失气者，必先硬后溏，不可攻之，攻之必腹满不能食也。欲饮水者，与水则哕，其后发热者，必大便硬而少也。以小承气汤和之，不转失气者，不可攻也。[46p]

Xiao Chengqi Decoction treats Taiyang disease. After vomiting and purging, if sweating occurs with mild restlessness, and there is frequent urination with hard stools, it is appropriate to use. For Yangming disease, if there is excessive sweating and mild aversion to cold, it indicates the exterior is not yet resolved; do not administer it in such cases. If there is abdominal fullness with no bowel movement, it can be given in small amounts.

Ingredients:

  • Dahuang (rhizoma rhei) lightly roasted, 1 tael
  • Zhi Shi (fructus aurantii) roasted, 1 tael
  • Hou Po (cortex magnoliae) prepared, 0.5 tael

Crush the ingredients and decoct them. For Yangming disease with tidal fever and slightly hard stools, Dai Chengqi Decoction can be given; if not hard, do not administer it. If there has been no bowel movement for six to seven days, there may be dry stool. To assess, administer a small amount of Xiao Chengqi Decoction; if there is a sensation of gas movement in the abdomen, this indicates dry stool, and it can be purged. If there is no gas movement, there will certainly be hard stools followed by diarrhea; don't purge, as it will lead to abdominal fullness and inability to eat.

If the patient desires water, and consuming water causes belching, followed by fever, this indicates stools are hard and sparse. Steep with Xiao Chengqi Decoction; if there is no gas movement, do not purge.[46p]

　　大承气汤　治刚痓胸满内实，口噤咬牙，大热渴，大便秘濇。　　大黄　芒硝各半两　厚朴姜炒　枳实各一两　　右判，每服三钱，姜三片，水一盏，煎七分，空心服。
　　四顺饮　治小儿血脉壅实，脏腑生热，颊赤多渴，五心烦躁，睡卧不安，四肢惊掣；及因乳哺不时，寒温失度，令儿血气不顺，肠胃不调，小便少，大便濇；或温病迟滞，欲成伏热；或壮热不歇，欲发惊癎。又治风热结核，头面疮疖，目赤咽痛，疮疹毒一切壅滞，并宜服之。　　赤芍药　当归　生甘草　大黄各一两　　右銼散，三岁以上每服二钱，水一盏，煎至七分，作两服。一方，名四顺散，加薄荷二叶为引。欲利小便，加白茯苓。虚热加甘草。不利加大黄。冒风邪加去节麻黄。中风体强，眼睛上视，加独活。量儿大小虚实加减，微溏利为度。[47p]

Da Chengqi Decoction treats severe abdominal fullness with real internal heat, clenching of the jaw, intense thirst, and constipation.

Ingredients:

  • Rhubarb and Glauber's salt, both half a tael
  • Aushuang, ginger (stir-fried), and bitter orange, each one tael

Usage: Mix the above, taking three qian each time, adding three slices of ginger, with one cup of water, simmering down to seven parts, and take it on an empty stomach.

Si Shun Drink treats the obstruction of blood vessels in children, internal heat in the organs, red cheeks with thirst, restlessness in the five heart areas, disturbed sleep, and spasms in the limbs. This may arise from irregular breastfeeding, improper temperatures causing blood and Qi imbalance, poor digestion, reduced urination, and constipation. It also addresses lingering febrile diseases, possible heat accumulation, or persistent fever leading to convulsions, as well as treating wind-heat syndromes like skin ulcers, red eyes, sore throat, and other obstructive toxins.

Ingredients:

  • Red peony root, Angelica, raw licorice, and rhubarb, each one tael

Usage: Grind and disperse. For children over three, take two qian each time with one cup of water, simmer until reduced to seven parts, divided into two doses. There is another formula called Si Shun San, which adds two leaves of peppermint for guidance. To promote urination, add white poria. For heat conditions, add licorice. For poor digestion, add rhubarb. For wind-cold invasions, remove the jointed ephedra. For strong body types with upward eye gazing, add notopterygium. Adjust the dosage according to the child's size, condition, and needs, ensuring a mild laxative effect.[47p]

　　小柴胡汤　治伤寒温热病，身热恶风，颈项强急，胸胁满痛，呕吐哕逆，烦渴，寒热往来，身面皆黄，小便不利，大便秘濇；或过经不解；或潮热不除；及瘥后劳复发热，疼痛烦热；经血适来适去，寒热如疟。　　人参　甘草炙　黄芩各三钱　柴胡八钱　半夏汤泡七次，焙干，二钱半　　右銼散，每服二钱，水一盏，生姜三片，枣一枚，煎七分，去滓温服，不拘时。[48p]

Xiao Chai Hu Decoction is used to treat febrile diseases caused by cold, characterized by fever and aversion to wind, stiffness and pain in the neck, fullness and pain in the chest and sides, vomiting and belching, thirst, alternating chills and fever, yellowing of the body and face, difficulty urinating, and constipation. It may also address conditions such as unresolved menstrual flow, persistent fever from unresolved malaria, and the return of fever and pain after recovery; or irregularity of menstrual blood, with symptoms resembling malaria.

Ingredients:

  • 3 qian (a traditional unit of weight) each of ginseng, roasted licorice, and yellow cortex
  • 8 qian of bupleurum
  • 2.5 qian of half summer, soaked in decoction seven times and then dried

Preparation: Grind the above into a powder. For each dose, take 2 qian with one cup of water, add three slices of fresh ginger and one jujube, then simmer until reduced by half. Strain and take warm, without regard to timing.[48p]

　　桂枝汤　治太阳中风，阳浮而阴弱，阳浮热自发，阴弱者汗自出，啬啬恶寒，翕翕发热，鼻鸣干呕者。　　桂枝去皮　生姜　芍药各一两半　炙草一两　枣子六个　　右为饮子，每服三钱，水一盏，煎至八分，去滓，大小加减。服须臾，嗓热粥一盏以助药力，温覆，令一时许。通身热微，微似有汗者，加减桂枝汤。自西北二方居人，四时行之，无不应验。江淮间，惟冬及春可行。自春末及夏至已前，桂枝证，加黄芩一分，谓之阴旦汤。夏至后有桂枝证，可加知母半两，石膏一两，或升麻一分。若病素虚寒者，止用古方，不在加减也。戒曰：桂枝最难用。虽云表不解，可发汗，宜桂枝汤，须是病人常自汗出，小便不数，手足温和，或手足指梢作微冷，少须却温，身虽微似烦而又憎寒，始可行之。若病人身无汗，小便数，或手足冷不恶寒，或饮酒家不喜甘者，慎不可行桂枝也。仍有桂枝证，服汤已，无桂枝证者，尤不可再与。[49p]

Guizhi Decoction is used to treat a Taiyang wind condition, characterized by a floating yang and weak yin. When the yang is floating and heat arises, the weak yin leads to spontaneous sweating, aversion to cold, and intermittent feverish sensations, along with nasal congestion and dry retching.

The ingredients include:

  • 1.5 taels of cinnamon twig (桂枝) without the bark
  • 1.5 taels of fresh ginger (生姜)
  • 1.5 taels of peony root (芍药)
  • 1 tael of honey-fried licorice root (炙草)
  • 6 dates (枣子)

This mixture is prepared into a decoction. Each dose is 3 qian, with a cup of water, boiled down to around 80%, then filtered. Adjust the dosage as needed. After taking the decoction, it is advised to consume a bowl of warm congee to enhance the medicinal effects, covering oneself well for about an hour. If there is a slight overall warmth and mild sweating, then the Guizhi Decoction may be further adjusted.

For those residing in the northwest and in all seasons, this remedy will certainly prove effective. In the Jianghuai region, it should only be used in winter and spring. From late spring to just before summer solstice, when there are symptoms of Guizhi, you may add one part of Huangqin, calling it Yindan Decoction. After the summer solstice, if there are Guizhi symptoms, half a tael of Zhimu and one tael of gypsum, or one part of Shengma may be added.

However, if the patient has long-standing deficiency and cold conditions, only the original formula should be used without adjustments.

A caution: Guizhi is the most difficult herb to use. Although it is said to resolve external conditions, it can induce sweating. The suitable case for Guizhi Decoction requires that the patient typically has spontaneous sweating, urination is infrequent, hands and feet are warm, perhaps with slight cold in hands and toes, and mildly bothersome body heat with aversion to cold. In such cases, it can be used. If the patient has no sweating, more frequent urination, cold hands and feet without aversion to cold, or if the individual dislikes sweet due to alcohol consumption, Guizhi should not be used. Moreover, if the symptoms of Guizhi have been present and the decoction was taken without resolution of those symptoms, it should not be administered again.[49p]

　　桂枝加芍药汤　治太阳病，反下之，因腹痛，是有表复有里，宜服。　　桂枝　生姜各一两半　芍药三两半，利者先煎　大枣六个　甘草炙，一两　　右(口父)咀，水煎，加减服。痛甚者加大黄，大实者加一两半，羸瘦虚弱者减之。

Cinnamon Twig Decoction with Rhubarb is used for Taiyang disease; if there is a reversal with abdominal fullness and pain belonging to Taiyin, the formula Cinnamon Twig Decoction with Peony is indicated; for severe pain in a robust person, Cinnamon Twig Decoction with Rhubarb is indicated.

　　四逆汤　治阴证伤寒，自利不渴，呕哕不止，吐利俱作，小便或濇或利，脉微欲绝，腹痛胀满，手足厥冷，或咳或悸，内寒外热，下利清谷，四肢沉重，或汗出热不解，内拘急，身疼痛而恶寒者，用此方治之。　　干姜一两半　附子一个，生用　生甘草一两　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，用水一盏，煎七分，不拘时冷服。
　　理中汤　治脾胃不和，中塞上冲，胸胁逆满，心腹(疒丂)痛，痰逆恶心呕吐，心下虚烦痞满，膈塞不通，饮食减少，短气羸困。温中逐水，止邪汗，去湿。泄泻注下，水谷不分，腹中雷鸣；伤寒时气，里寒外热，霍乱吐利，手足厥伶，胸痹心痛，逆气短气，寒多不饮水吐者。　　人参去芦　白朮　干姜炮，各三两　炙草一两半　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，水一盏，煎六分，去滓带热服，空心食前；或研细末白汤调下。[51p]

Si Ni Decoction is used to treat cold damage with yin symptoms, characterized by diarrhea without thirst, persistent vomiting, simultaneous vomiting and diarrhea, urination that may be clear or frequent, a pulse that is weak and about to fade, abdominal pain and fullness, cold hands and feet, possible cough or palpitations, internal cold with external heat, diarrhea of clear liquid, heavy limbs, possible sweating without relief from heat, internal cramping, body aches with chills. The formula consists of:

  • Dried ginger: 1.5 taels
  • Aconite: 1 piece, raw
  • Raw licorice: 1 tael

Crush the ingredients, take 3 qian each time, using 1 cup of water, and decoct to 7 parts, taking it cold regardless of time.

Li Zhong Decoction treats disharmony of the spleen and stomach, with phlegm obstructing ascending qi, fullness in the chest and ribs, heart and abdominal pain, phlegm reversing that causes nausea and vomiting, a feeling of weakness and fullness below the heart, obstructed diaphragm, reduced appetite, shortness of breath, and fatigue. It warms the center, expels water, stops excessive sweating, and removes dampness. Symptoms may include diarrhea with undifferentiated water and food, rumbling in the abdomen; during cold damage, internal cold with external heat, cholera with vomiting and diarrhea, cold hands and feet, chest tightness with heart pain, reversed qi and shortness of breath, and those with excessive cold who cannot drink water and vomit. The formula includes:

  • Ginseng (with husk removed): 3 taels
  • White atractylodes: 3 taels
  • Dried ginger (processed): 3 taels
  • Honey-fried licorice: 1.5 taels

Crush the ingredients, take 3 qian each time, using 1 cup of water, and decoct to 6 parts, straining the dregs and taking it warm, on an empty stomach before meals, or grind into a fine powder and mix with warm white soup.[51p]

腹痛者，加人参一两半。寒多，加干姜一两半。渴者，加白朮一两半。脐上筑者，肾气动也，去白朮，加肉桂四两。吐多者，去白朮，加生姜三两。下多者，还用白朮。悸者，加茯苓二两。或四肢拘急，腹满下利转筋者，去白朮，加附子一个生用，末之，蜜丸如鸡子黄大，名理中丸，又名调中丸。治厥阴脏寒，蛔上入膈，吐长虫，或胃中虚冷，因发汗故吐虫。先服理中丸，或加枳实、茯苓，蜜丸。治伤寒结胸欲绝，心膈高起，实满作痛，手不得近，并用热汤化下。[52p]

For those with abdominal pain, add one and a half taels of ginseng. If there is excessive cold, add one and a half taels of dried ginger. For those who are thirsty, add one and a half taels of white atractylodes. If there is swelling above the navel, it indicates movement of kidney Qi; remove the white atractylodes and add four taels of cinnamon. For excessive vomiting, remove the white atractylodes and add three taels of fresh ginger. For excessive diarrhea, use the white atractylodes again. For palpitations, add two taels of fu ling. If there are tightness in the limbs, abdominal fullness, diarrhea, and cramping, remove the white atractylodes and add one piece of fresh aconite, ground into a powder, then mixed with honey to form pills the size of a quail egg, named Li Zhong Wan, also known as Tiao Zhong Wan. This treats cold in the Jueyin organ, when roundworms rise into the diaphragm, causing the expulsion of long worms, or when there is cold and emptiness in the stomach, resulting in the expulsion of worms due to sweating. First, take Li Zhong Wan, or add bitter orange and fu ling, mixed with honey to form pills. This treats cold damage leading to chest fullness and severe distress, with the heart's area elevated, feeling full and painful, where the hands cannot approach, and use hot soup to disperse.[52p]

　　大柴胡汤　治伤寒十余日，邪气结在里，往来寒热，邪实太盛，大便秘濇，腹满胀痛，谵语，心中痞硬，饮食不下，或不大便五六日，绕脐刺痛，时发烦躁；及汗后如疟，日晚发热，兼脏腑实，脉有力者可服。　　柴胡去芦，八钱　黄芩炒　赤芍药各三钱　枳实去穰麸炒，五钱　半夏泡七次切片焙，半两　　右銼散，姜枣煎加减服之。欲下，加大黄半两。

Da Chai Hu Decoction: For treating typhoid fever lasting more than ten days, when pathogenic qi is confined within, presenting alternating chills and fever, with excessive pathogen, severe constipation, abdominal fullness and pain, delirium, hardness in the heart, inability to eat or not defecating for five to six days, sharp pain around the navel, and occasional irritability; if after sweating it resembles malaria, with afternoon fever, and a fullness in the organs, and a strong pulse, it can be taken.

Ingredients: Chai Hu (without the pulp), 8 qian; Huang Qin (stir-fried), Chi Shao (each 3 qian); Zhi Shi (without the seed, stir-fried), 5 qian; Ban Xia (soaked seven times, sliced and dried), 2.5 qian. Grind and mix the above. Decoct with ginger and jujubes, adjust as needed. To promote bowel movement, add 2.5 qian Da Huang.

Yin Dan Decoction: For treating typhoid fever with pain in the limbs and joints, internal cold, external heat, and a feeling of weakness and restlessness.

Ingredients: Rou Gui (2 liang), Zhi Gan Cao (1 liang), Gan Jiang (prepared), Shao Yao, Huang Qin (each 1.5 liang). Grind these and take 3 qian each time with 1 cup of water and 1 jujube. Decoct, strain, and take warm to induce slight sweating.

Bai Hu Plus Ren Shen Decoction: For treating typhoid fever, particularly after vomiting or diarrhea, where after seven to eight days there's no resolution, and heat is trapped within, both internally and externally warm, with occasional chills, great thirst, excessive sweating, and persistent thirst without relief, with a strong pulse.

Ingredients: Shi Gao (4 liang, finely ground), Zhi Mu (1.5 liang), Jing Mi (1 sheng), Ren Shen, Zhi Gan Cao (each 2.5 qian). Grind these and take 3 qian each time with 1 cup of water, decoct until the rice is well-cooked, then consume.[53p]

Xiao Jian Zhong Decoction treats cold damage with a weak yang pulse and a wiry yin pulse, indicated by sudden abdominal pain. First, administer Xiao Jian Zhong Decoction.

Ingredients:

  • 1.5 taels of cinnamon twig
  • 3 taels of peony root
  • 2 taels of honey-fried licorice

Tuo Jia San - This remedy treats infants and young children suffering from cold-induced fever, with symptoms such as a heavy head and mind, lack of appetite, alternating between surprise and hunger, chills and fever, obstructed bowel movements, whether red or white, irritability and thirst, excessive cold sweat, accumulation and stagnation, fullness and urgency in the abdomen, a thin and sallow body, and high fever day and night. It is also suitable for treating wind strikes, cold-induced ailments, summer heat issues, convulsions, adverse reactions, and heat-related conditions affecting muscles, bones, kidneys, and other organs.

Ingredients:

  • 9 grams of prepared Angelica (Danggui) wine-washed
  • 9 grams of white Poria (Baifuling)
  • 9 grams of Gentian root (Longdancao), with the bulk removed
  • 6 grams of ginseng (Ren Shen), with the bulk removed
  • 6 grams of Bupleurum (Chai Hu)
  • 6 grams of Sichuan lovage (Chuanxiong)
  • 6 grams of Anemarrhena (ZhimMu), with the hair removed
  • 12 grams of honey-fried licorice (Gancao)

Grind the above into a fine powder. For each dose, take 3 grams with one cup of water, along with a piece of green onion (1 inch long), and boil until reduced to half a cup. Take warm, without time constraint. This formula releases heat and supports the exterior to restore internal balance. It prevents excessive sweating due to exterior weakness and resolves internal heat to ensure unimpeded energy. It opens the meridians externally and the pathways internally, facilitating smooth circulation without blocking the organs. It is effective for heat symptoms both externally and internally.[55p]

　　葶苈丸　治食乳冲脾，咳嗽伤风，面赤痰盛，身热喘嗽急促，化痰宽气进食。　　葶苈子隔纸略炒　汉防己　黑牵牛略炒　杏仁去皮尖双仁者，同干面炒黄，别捣，各一两　　右为末，研入杏膏拌匀，取蒸枣肉和，再捣为剂，丸如麻子大，每服五丸至七丸，淡姜汤下，乳食后，或临睡夜服。量大小加减。[56p]

Tingli Pills are used to treat food stagnation affecting the spleen, coughs due to cold, flushed face with excessive phlegm, feverish body with wheezing and rapid breathing, helping to transform phlegm, relieve qi, and aid in digestion.

　　麻黄汤　治伤寒头疼发热，身痛恶风无汗而喘。又治太阳病脉浮紧，无汗发热，身疼痛八九日不解，表证仍在，此当发其汗。服药已，其人烦热目瞑剧者，必衄，衄乃解。所以然者，阳气重故也。　　甘草生用，半两　麻黄去节，二两　桂枝一两　杏仁去皮尖，三十个　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，水一盏，煎八分，去滓大小加减服，被覆取汗。夏至后，须加知母、石膏各一两，黄芩八钱。盖麻黄性热，夏月温之，必有发黄发斑之失。凡伤寒热病，药性须凉，不可太温。惟冬及春或病人素虚寒者，乃用正方，不在加减例。

Mahuang Decoction treats typhoid with headache, fever, body aches, aversion to wind, and shortness of breath without sweating. It also treats the Taiyang disease where the pulse is floating and tight, no sweating, a fever, and body aches lasting eight to nine days without resolution, while the exterior symptoms remain; in this case, it should induce sweating. After taking the medicine, if the person becomes agitated, has a high fever, and closes their eyes violently, they are likely to have a nosebleed, and the nosebleed indicates resolution. This is because of the heaviness of Yang Qi.

Ingredients:

  • Licorice, raw, 15 grams
  • Ephedra, removed from the stems, 60 grams
  • Cinnamon twig, 30 grams
  • Apricot kernel, peeled and tipped, 30 pieces

Prepare as follows: Take the above ingredients and grind. For each dose, take 9 grams, boil in one cup of water until reduced to two-fifths, strain, and adjust dosage based on individual response to induce sweating. After the summer solstice, one should add 30 grams each of Anemarrhena and Gypsum, and 24 grams of Huangqin. This is because the nature of Ephedra is hot; in summer, warming it may lead to yellowing and spots. In all cases of febrile diseases, the properties of medicine must be cool, and should not be too warming. Only in winter and spring, or for patients who are generally deficient and cold, should one use the standard method without adjustments.

Preparation: Grind the right ingredients to powder. Each dose is three qian, with a cup of water and decocted until reduced to seven parts, to be taken warm. If there is slight diarrhea, remove Mahuang and add a ball-sized piece of Rhae blossoms, stir-fried until red. If there is choking, remove Mahuang and add half a qian of Fuzi (prepared). If urination is difficult, remove Mahuang and add one tael of Fuling. If wheezing occurs, remove Mahuang and add half a tael of peeled Xingren. If there is thirst, remove half a tael of Banhxia and add one and a half taels of Guaoluo root.[62p]

　　柴胡石膏汤　治时行瘟疫，壮热恶风，头痛体疼，鼻塞咽干，心胸烦满，寒热往来，痰实咳嗽，涕唾稠粘。　　柴胡五两　黄芩三两　半夏　甘草各二两半　石膏一斤　知母六两　粳米六合　　右銼，每服二钱，水一盏，生姜二斤，淡豆豉十粒，煎至七分，去滓稍热服。小儿分作三服，不拘时。无汗，加麻黄、半夏、五味子。
　　天麻防风丸　治一切惊风，身体壮热，多睡惊悸，手足抽掣，精神昏愦，咳嗽痰涎不利，及风温邪热，并宜服之。　　明天麻　防风　人参　辰砂研飞　雄黄　甘草炙，各一钱　麝香　牛黄各一分　全蝎炒　僵蚕炒，各半两　　右为末，炼蜜丸如梧桐子大，每服一丸至二丸，薄荷汤下，不拘时。[63p]

Chaihu Shigao Decoction is used to treat seasonal epidemics with strong fever, aversion to wind, headaches, body aches, nasal congestion, dry throat, chest fullness, alternating chills and fever, phlegm-heavy cough, and thick and sticky nasal mucus.

Ingredients:

  • Chaihu (Bupleurum) 5 taels
  • Huangqin (Scutellaria) 3 taels
  • Banxia (Pinellia) 2.5 taels
  • Gancao (Licorice) 2.5 taels
  • Shigao (Gypsum) 1 pound
  • Zhimhu (Anemarrhena) 6 taels
  • Jingmi (Glutinous Rice) 6 taels

Prepare by grinding these ingredients. When taking, use 2 qian (a weightunit), with one cup of water, 2 jin of fresh ginger, and 10 pieces of fermented soybeans. Boil until reduced by a third, strain, and take while warm. For children, divide into three doses, with no specific timing. If there is no sweating, add Mahuang (Ephedra), Banxia, and Wuweizi (Schisandra).

Tianma Fangfeng Pill is used to treat all kinds of seizures, strong body heat, excessive sleep with palpitations, convulsions in hands and feet, confusion of spirit, cough with troublesome phlegm, and also for wind-heat pathogens, which is also appropriate to take.

Ingredients:

  • Tianma (Gastrodia)
  • Fangfeng (Siler)
  • Ren Shen (Ginseng)
  • Chen Sha (Cinnabar) finely ground
  • Xionghuang (Realgar)
  • Gancao (Licorice) roasted, each 1 qian
  • Shexiang (Musk) and Niu Huang (Cattle Gallstone) each 1 fen
  • Quanxie (Scorpion) and Jiang Can (Silkworm) both roasted, each half tael

Grind these into a fine powder and make pills the size of Chinese phoenix tree seeds. Take 1 to 2 pills with mint decoction, with no specific timing.[63p]

　　化风丹　凉风化痰，退热定搐。

Gold Foaming Herb Powder: Treats wind injury with excessive phlegm, dizziness and headache, stiff neck, chills and fever alternating, body aches, chest fullness and pain, cough with wheezing, and thick, sticky phlegm. It is especially effective against sudden cold epidemics, overwhelming heat, and aversion to wind.
Ingredients:

  • Schizonepeta spikes (荆芥穗), four taels
  • Front Hush (前胡)
  • Ephedra (麻黄) (remove joints)
  • Inula Flowers (旋覆花)
  • Honey-fried Licorice (甘草炙), each three taels
  • Ban Xia (半夏) prepared
  • Red Peony (赤芍药), each one tael.
    Grind these into powder. Take two qian with a cup of water, two slices of ginger, and one date, decoct for six minutes, remove residue and take warm, regardless of time. If cold evil is present, add apricot seeds and five flavors.

Also applicable for treating cold damage, phlegm in the middle burner leading to strong heat and headache, tight pulse, and intermittent chills and fevers that resemble wind injury, but without headache indicates a different condition.
Ingredients:

  • Front Hush (前胡) and Inula Flowers (旋覆花), each three taels
  • Schizonepeta spikes (荆芥穗), four taels
  • Red Poria (赤茯苓)

  • Ban Xia (半夏) (washed and prepared), each one tael.

　　三拗汤　治感冒风邪，鼻塞声重，语音不出；或伤风伤冷，头疼目眩，四肢拘急，咳嗽多痰，胸满气短。　　麻黄不去节　杏仁不去皮尖　生草生用，各等分　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，水一盏，生姜三片，煎至六分，去滓温服，取汗为度。一方加荆芥、桔梗。嗽甚，加五味子、细辛各减半。一方，麻黄去节，杏仁去皮尖，甘草炙，名三和汤，治喘嗽尤妙。有热加前胡。伤风加荆芥。有痰加半夏。
　　和解汤　治小儿四时感冒寒邪，壮热烦躁，鼻塞多涕，惊悸自汗，肢体疼痛，及疮疹已发未发，皆可服。　　羌活　防风　川芎　人参各一两　干葛　升麻　生甘草　芍药各半两　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，水一盏，生姜一片，枣一个，煎至六分，不拘时服。无汗加麻黄。欬嗽者，加杏仁、五味子、桔梗。[65p]

Three-Ingredient Decoction: Used to treat cold-induced conditions with nasal congestion and heavy voice, resulting in inability to speak; or pain from wind-cold with symptoms such as headache, dizziness, painful limbs, and cough with phlegm, leading to chest fullness and shortness of breath.

Ingredients:

  • Ephedra (Mahuang), without nodes
  • Apricot kernels (Xingren), without skin tips
  • Fresh licorice (Gancao), of equal parts

Method: Grind and prepare; take three qian (a unit of weight) each time, with one cup of water, three slices of fresh ginger, and boil until reduced to six parts. Strain and take warm, aiming for sweating as a measure. For additional variation, add Schizonepeta (Jingjie) and Balloon flower (Jiegeng). If coughing severely, add Schisandra (Wuweizi) and Asarum (Xixin), each in half quantity. Another variation is to remove the nodes from Ephedra, use peeled apricot kernels, and fried licorice, called the "Three Harmonizing Decoction," which is particularly effective for cough and wheezing. If there is heat, add the previous Hu (Qianhu). For wind-cold, add Schizonepeta. If phlegm is present, add Pinellia (Banxia).

Harmonizing Decoction: Used for treating children's seasonal colds with cold evil, causing strong heat and restlessness, nasal congestion with excessive mucus, palpitations with spontaneous sweating, body aches, and rashes whether they have emerged or not.

Ingredients:

  • Notopterygium (Qianghuo), one liang (about 30 grams)
  • Saposhnikovia (Fangfeng), one liang
  • Ligusticum (Chuanxiong), one liang
  • Ginseng (Renshen), one liang
  • Dried Kudzu (Gegen), half a liang
  • Cimicifuga (Shengma), half a liang
  • Fresh licorice (Gancao), half a liang
  • Peony (Shaoyao), half a liang

Method: Grind and prepare; take three qian each time, with one cup of water, one slice of fresh ginger, and one jujube, and boil until reduced to six parts. Does not have a specific time for consumption. If there is no sweating, add Ephedra. For cough, add peeled apricot kernels, Schisandra, and Balloon flower.[65p]

Huo Xiang Zheng Qi San - Treats children's typhoid with vomiting and diarrhea. Ingredients: Huo Xiang, Bai Zhu, Hou Po, Chen Pi, Ban Xia, Bai Fu (white), Bai Zhi, Jie Geng, Da Fu Pi, Su Ye, Gan Cao. Grind them together, add three slices of fresh ginger, and decoct them slowly for consumption. If sweating occurs, use Cang Zhu and omit Bai Zhu.

Bu Yang Tang - Treats children's severe cold symptoms in early winter, with blue veins in the Ming Tang (the space between the eyebrows), dark blue complexion on the forehead, swollen blue veins at the back of the head, blue lips, white and slippery tongue, hoarseness and wheezing in the throat, slightly blue stools, cold tips of ears, watery eyes with frequent tears, excessive eye mucus, discomfort in the chest, frequent fright during sleep, no spasms but cold. Ingredients: Chai Hu, Sheng Ma, Ma Huang, Gui Shen (returning herbs) each three qian; Di Long five qian; a little scorpion tail; Sheng Di, Wu Zhu Yu each five fen; Huang Qi two fen; Chen Pi one fen; Ge Gen, Lian Qiao, Huang Bo, Gan Cao each one qian. The above is made into a coarse powder, one dose mixed with a cup of water, decocted as usual. Take after meals while warm, gradually promoting sleep, boosting spirit, harmonizing Qi, and enhancing digestion.[66p]

Yin Bai San: Used for treating strong fever from typhoid, headaches, body aches, with a strong pulse and abdominal distension. If sweating accompanies fright, it can also be taken. Combine half a pound of cold water stone, calcine it, and grind it into a very fine powder. Add one and a half qian of fried ginger and turmeric, mix well; if it appears diluted, add a bit more for color. Each dose is one qian, taken with ginger soup. If unable to drink, apply a thick mixture on the lips and take with milk at any time.

Gan Lu San: Used for treating strong fever from typhoid, headache, body pain, to release the exterior and induce sweating, especially for those with high fever. The formula consists of two liang of cassia borate, ground finely; half a liang of licorice. Mix well and take one qian with thickly boiled radish soup. One variation includes half a liang of saposhnikovia.

Xiang Ke Wan: Used for treating fullness and discomfort in the heart and chest due to typhoid. Use mandarin peel, the quantity is not strict. Grind into a fine powder. Each dose is one qian, taken with ginger soup before meals.

Xiao Zhen Zhu Wan: Used for phlegm obstruction, sore throat, cough relief, stopping irritability and clearing the mind. Wash half a sheng of pinellia seven times; dry and grind into powder. Combine one liang of burn-dried white alum and one liang of calcined cold water stone, both ground into powder. Mix well and form into fine paste for pills, using equal amounts of millet, sesame seeds, and broad beans. Each dose ranges from five to seven to ten pills, taken with warm ginger soup after meals, adjusting the quantity as needed.[67p]

　　右入蜜一钱，调匀，服无时。

Right: Finely grind, using half a cup of cow's milk, and simmer until reduced to two-thirds. Strain, let cool, and take three to four spoonfuls at any time.

Lotus Root Juice and Honey: Treats fever and thirst from cold damage.
Crush half a cup of fresh lotus root to extract juice,
then add one qian of honey, mix well, and consume at any time.

Kudzu Root Decoction: Treats cold damage with fever and thirst.
Kudzu root and ginseng, each half a liang;
Ophiopogon removed from the heart, white poria, roasted licorice, and alisma, each one fen.
Grind these into powder, take half a qian or one qian at a time, add half a cup of water and two peppermint leaves, simmer until reduced to one-third, strain, and take warm at any time.

Lily Powder: Treats abdominal fullness and pain from cold damage.
Roasted lily, half a liang.
Grind into powder, take half a qian at a time, and mix with rice drink for consumption at any time.

Huangqin Powder: Treats cold damage lasting five to six days with constipation and heat-induced agitation.
Huangqin, Zhi Qiao (fructus aurantii) prepared by frying, da huang (rhubarb), and big belly fruit, each half a liang.
Grind these into coarse powder, take one qian at a time, add half a cup of water, simmer until reduced to one-third, strain, and consume without regard to time.

Rhinoceros Horn Powder: Treats the same conditions as above.
Rhinoceros horn shavings, da huang prepared by blasting, and chih hu, each half a liang; ginseng one fen; natron and licorice, each half fen.
Grind into powder, take half a qian at a time, mix with five fen of water and one jujube, simmer until reduced to one-third, strain, and take warm, adjusting the quantity as needed.[70p]

　　石燕散　治伤寒小便不通，小腹胀满。　　石燕火煅为末

　　萱草根

　　蒲黄炒黑

Shiyan San: Treats febrile diseases with urinary retention and abdominal distension.
Stone swallow, fire-calcined and ground to a powder.
Mix with scallion white soup and take as needed, without specific timing.

Another formula:
Hemerocallis root, decocted into a soup, mix with Wuling San to take before breastfeeding.

Kudzu root juice: Treats febrile diseases with persistent nosebleeds.
Fresh kudzu juice, a small cup, divided into three to four doses as needed, without specific timing.

Liding San: Treats similarly.
Phragmites pollen, dry kudzu root powder, dried pomegranate flower powder, each one part.
Grind to a fine powder, take half a qian or one dose, mixed with fresh Rehmannia juice, take two or three doses as needed, without specific timing.

Another formula:
Fried Phragmites pollen, ground to a powder, take half a qian or one dose, mixed with freshly drawn water, as needed, without specific timing.

Golden honey juice: Treats febrile diseases with prolonged nosebleeds.
Fresh Rehmannia juice, Sichuan honey, each half a small cup, Phragmites pollen, half a tael.
Mix well, slightly fry, take half a cup or a little more as needed, without specific timing.

Shenbai San: Treats febrile diseases with symptoms of blood vomiting, nosebleeds, coughing up blood, and blood in urination and defecation.
Sophora flower, one part, slightly fried; fatty powder, half a tael.
Grind to a fine powder, take one qian or half a qian, decoct with willow branch soup and let it cool before taking. If unable to prepare this, simply grind willow branches to powder and mix with fresh water, then take.[71p]

Xiang Mo Wan: Treats chills and fever with hemorrhaging; suitable for young children who cannot take powdered medicine. Finely grind ink into a powder. Take the mixture formed into balls the size of millet; each time use seven balls, to be taken with water or administered.

Di Huang Juice: Treats chills and fever with vomiting blood, chest discomfort, and continuous thirst; also treats hemorrhaging. Extract juice from fresh Rehmannia.

Mai Men Dong Decoction: Treats chills and fever with cough and wheezing. Ingredients include: Mai Men Dong (Ophiopogon) – 1 tael, Ginseng – 1 tael, Purple Aster – 1 tael (washed and dried), Cinnamon heart – half a tael, Licorice – 1 fen. Grind these into a powder; then add 20 almonds, roasted with their skin removed, ground fine and mixed well. Take 1 qian with 1 cup of water and 2 slices of ginger; decoct until reduced to 6 parts, strain and take warm at any time.

Yi Nian Jin San: Treats chills and fever with cough due to wind-heat. Ingredients: White Silkworm (without silk mouth) – 1 qian, Licorice – half a tael, Corydalis – 1 fen. Grind these into a fine powder; every time take a pinch mixed with juice, at any time.

Run Fei San: Treats chills and fever with nasal congestion, phlegm accumulation causing cough, lung qi obstruction, and rendered speechlessness. Ingredients: Ephedra (remove root segments) – 1 tael, Ginseng (remove coarse parts) – 1 tael, Almonds (roasted and skin removed) – 1 tael, Fritillaria (roasted to yellow) – 1 tael, Honey-fried Licorice – half a tael, Aged Tangerine Peel – 1.5 fen, Platycodon (remove coarse parts) – 1 tael, Gelatin (fried to pearl size) – 1 fen. Grind these into a powder; every time take 1 qian with 8 parts of water, decoct until reduced to 6 parts, strain and take warm at any time.[72p]

　　赤芍药散　治伤寒阳证咳逆。
　　赤芍药不拘多少，沸汤浸七遍，每遍以瓦盆盖少时，数足取出，炒燥为末　每服一钱，豆豉三粒，生姜一片，水七分，煎至五分，放温服，无时。
　　荜良汤　治伤寒，寒多咳逆。
　　荜澄茄　良姜各等分
　　右为末，每服一钱，水六分，煎数沸，入酢少许，搅匀带热服。
　　灵砂膏　治伤寒脉数，热入胃，呕吐。　　泽泻二两半　肉桂一两　猪苓　赤茯苓　白朮去芦，各一两半　朱砂细末，一钱　　右为末，炼蜜和膏鸡头大，每服一丸，生姜自然汁化破与服。只末用，便是五灵散。亦治发热烦渴饮水，水入即吐，或小便不利。积热在里发黄，浓前茵陈蒿汤调下。余病饮调。[73p]

Chi Shao Yao San - Treats warm diseases with yang symptoms and cough.

For Chi Shao Yao, regardless of amount, soak in boiling water seven times, each time covering with a pottery bowl for a short period. After steeping, take out and dry-fry to make a fine powder. Each dose is one qian, mixed with three grains of dou chi, one slice of fresh ginger, and seven parts water, decocted to five parts, cooled and taken at any time.

Bi Liang Tang - Treats warm diseases with cold symptoms and cough.

Ingredients: Bi Cheng Qie and Liang Jiang in equal parts.

Grind the above into a powder. Each dose is one qian, mixed with six parts water, decocted several times until boiling, then add a small amount of vinegar, stir well, and take while warm.

Ling Sha Gao - Treats warm diseases with rapid pulse, heat entering the stomach, and vomiting.

Ingredients: Ze Xie (2.5 liang), Rou Gui (1 liang), Zhu Ling, Chi Fu Ling, and Bai Zhu (without the husk), each at 1.5 liang; fine powder of Zhu Sha (1 qian).

Grind the ingredients into a powder, refine in honey to make a paste the size of a chicken head. Each dose is one pill, mixed with the natural juice of fresh ginger and taken. This powder also forms Wu Ling San. It treats fever, thirst with a desire to drink, urination difficulties, or vomiting upon drinking. Accumulated heat inside causing yellowing, can be addressed with Chong Huang Qian and adjustments with water for other ailments.[73p]

　　四味人参汤　治伤寒脉迟，胃冷呕吐。　　干姜炮　黄芩　黄连去须　人参各等分　　右为粗末，每服一钱，水六分，煎至四分，去滓温服，无时。

　　半夏汤　治伤寒呕逆，不下乳食，及干啘欲死。　　半夏半两，汤泡七次　生姜一两
　　右同銼碎焙干，每服一钱，水一盏，煎至五分，去滓时时与服，无时。

Four Flavor Ginseng Decoction: Treats typhoid with slow pulse and cold stomach causing vomiting.
Use equal parts of roasted dry ginger, Huangqin (Scutellaria), Huanglian (Coptis) after removing the roots, and ginseng. Grind them into coarse powder. Each dose is ten grams, boiled in six parts water until reduced to four parts. Strain and take warm, without restriction on timing.

Fuzi Jiangpu Pill: Treats typhoid with excessive cold and vomiting, cold hands and feet.
Use half a tael of prepared Fuzi (Aconitum) with skin and root removed, one part each of roasted dry ginger and Jiangpu (Magnolia bark). Grind these into powder, form into pills the size of sesame seeds. Take five to seven pills with rice drink, without restriction on timing.

Banxia Decoction: Treats typhoid with vomiting and inability to consume milk or food, and severe dry heaving.
Use half a tael of Banxia (Pinellia), soaked in broth seven times, and one tael of fresh ginger. Grind together, dry roast, and each dose is ten grams, boiled in one cup of water until reduced to five parts. Strain and take at regular intervals, without restriction on timing.

Lugen Drink: Treats typhoid with severe dry heaving and reverse stomach vomiting.
Chop fresh reed root, and use two parts each of green bamboo leaf, half a portion of glutinous rice, and half a tael of fresh ginger. Chew these and first boil with one liter of water until reduced to half a liter, then add the herbs and boil again, taking two to three portions as needed, adjusting the amount according to the size desired.[74p]

San Huang San treats yang jaundice caused by a febrile disease.
Take half a tael of Sichuan rhubarb, finely ground and lightly fried, and one-dram each of scutellaria, coptis. Mix and create a powder. For each dose, take half a qian with six fen of water. Boil until half remains, and take warm at any time.
Barley Sprout Juice treats as above.
Crush barley sprouts, then strain the juice and consume. Wheat sprouts may also be used.

Ren Shen Chai Hu Yin Zi treats body weakness due to cold pathogens, with symptoms of general heat, heaviness in the head and eyes, stiff neck and back, pain in the limbs, dry retching and nausea, alternating cold and heat, intermittent fevers, and thirst with no appetite.
Ingredients: ginseng, bupleurum, white atractylodes, white poria, green tangerine peel, platycodon, ophiopogon, Sichuan ligusticum, white peony, roasted licorice, mulberry bark, and spilanthus, each in equal parts. Mix to a powder. For each dosage, take one or two qian with one cup of water and one dried plum. Boil until six fen remain and take according to size, at any time.
Ji Bai Tiao San treats febrile diseases from cold, with symptoms resembling malaria, persistent without recovery, gradually turning into internal heat.
Ingredients: vermilion, burned alum, iron powder, powdered frost, lead white frost, each one qian; light powder, white fuzi, each two qian; six scorpion tails; small amounts of borneol and musk. Mix to a powder. For each dosage, take half a qian, mix with egg white and well water, approximately one teacup, blend together and consume at any time.[75p]

Yin Chen San: Treats the yellowing from typhoid fever; do not purgative.
Yin Chen: one tael, Bai Zhu: half a tael, Gan Cao: half a tael.
Prepare as a powder, take half a qian each dose, dissolved in boiling water. For those with difficulty urinating, add one tael of Fu Ling.

Jiang Xue Dan: Treats yellowing occurring five to six days after typhoid fever; with difficulty urinating, restlessness, heat and discomfort; drinking water does not relieve the agitation.
Zhu Sha: half a tael ground, Shui Fei Xiao Shi: two taels ground, Long Nao: a small amount.
Grind them together finely, mix with white rice to form pills the size of a chick's head. Swallow with sugar water, according to size of the dose.

Shang Lu San: Treats typhoid fever with swollen and painful throat.
Shang Lu root: chop finely and pound.
Fry it until cooked, wrap in a handkerchief and apply to the swollen area; change when it cools.

Gan Ju Fang Feng Tang: Treats swollen throat from typhoid fever.
Jie Geng: one tael, rice wash: soak and roast, Gan Cao and Fang Feng: each two taels, fried.
Grind into powder, take two qian with one bowl of water, boil down to six parts, let cool, and sip slowly.

Huang Bo Mi: Treats heat toxin from typhoid fever, causing sores and redness on the tongue and mouth.
Huang Bo: remove coarse skin.
Soak overnight in honey, lightly simmer and hold in the mouth, ensuring the juice does not stop; can also use powdered Huang Bo, simmer together and hold in the mouth.

Huang Qin Tang: Treats various conditions of the mouth and tongue caused by typhoid fever, such as yellow tongue, black tongue, swollen tongue, cracked tongue, needles appearing on the tongue, and bleeding from the tongue; also treats nosebleeds.
Huang Qin: three qian, Chi Shao Yao and Zhi Gan Cao: each two qian.[76p]

　　右(口父)咀，每二钱，水一盏，煎至六分，去滓温服。

　　黄连汤　治伤寒，热入肠胃，下痢脓血。　　黄连二两　黄蘗俱微炒　阿胶各一两，蛤粉炒　栀子仁半两　　右为粗末，每服一二钱，水六分，煎至四分，去滓温服，无时。[77p]

Take (the recipe), every two coins with one cup of water, boil until reduced to six parts, strain and take warm.

For treating wind-cold and chest obstruction:
Half a liang of rhubarb, stir-fried orange peel one liang. Grind to a fine powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of small coins. For chest obstruction, using half a qian of Glauber's salt and dissolving half a or one pill in ginger water for ingestion. For phlegm, boil tangerine peel in water and take as needed.

For treating cold-induced chest tightness and hard pain:
Two pieces of Aconite, one raw and one prepared. Grind together, mix with natural ginger juice to form pills the size of a chicken's head. Each pill is taken with honey water.

For treating febrile diseases and heat toxins in the chest, especially in critical condition for six or seven days:
Half a liang of bitter root, crushed, mixed with one cup of wine, boiled down to half a cup, strain and cool. Divide into three or four doses, take all at once until bile is vomited, immediate recovery.

For treating febrile diseases with heat entering the intestines, causing bloody diarrhea:
Two liang of Coptis, both slightly stir-fried, along with one liang each of donkey-hide gelatin, and stir-fried clam powder, half a liang of gardenia seeds. Grind to a coarse powder, taking one to two qians with six parts water, boil down to four parts, strain and take warm as needed.[77p]

　　栀子仁汤　治伤寒热毒，攻于肠胃，下赤汁，或如烂肉鸭肝，壮热腹痛。　　栀子仁二十一个　豉二合　薤白一握，切　　右以水二大盏，同煎至一盏，去滓，量大小，分作数服，无时。
　　乌仙散　治阴证伤寒，四肢厥逆。
　　川乌不拘多少
　　右以童便浸，不计日数，直至浸脱皮时，用水洗净切碎，晒至八分干；便以纸袋盛，悬于当风处，用时旋取为未，腊茶调下半钱，量大小及病势与之。
　　烧附散　治伤寒阴盛隔阳，身冷厥逆，脉沉细而烦躁体冷。　　大附子一枚，半两重者
　　右入急火烧，微存中心二三分取出，用磁器合盖，放冷为末，更入腊茶末一钱，同研匀细，每服半钱，水一小盏，蜜少许同煎半盏，去滓温服。服讫，须臾躁止得睡，汗出而解。一方烧附末，每一字或半钱，酒调下，频服取汗出瘥。小儿本怯者，最宜服。[78p]

Gardenia Seed Decoction: For treating febrile illness with toxic heat, attacking the intestines and stomach, resulting in red discharge, or resembling rotten flesh or duck liver, leading to strong heat and abdominal pain.

Ingredients: 21 Gardenia seeds, 2 cups of fermented soybeans, a handful of garlic chives, chopped.

Boil with 2 large cups of water until reduced to 1 cup, strain, and divide the dosage based on individual size and condition; can be taken at any time.

Wuxian Powder: For treating yin syndrome of febrile illness and extremities becoming cold and reversed.

Ingredients: No fixed quantity of Chuanwu (a type of medicinal herb).

Soak in child’s urine without counting days, until the skin peels off, then wash, chop finely, and sun-dry until 80% dry. Store in a paper bag hung in a windy place. When needed, take a small amount, mix with half a penny weight of aged tea, adjusted according to size and severity of the condition.

Burning Fu Powder: For treating febrile illness with excessive yin obstructing yang, causing body to feel cold with reversed extremities, pulse to feel deep and thin, restlessness accompanied by cold body.

Ingredients: 1 piece of large fuzi, weighing half a tael.

Introduce it to a quick fire until slightly charred in the center, then take it out, grinding it while it is still warm in a covered pottery pot. Once cooled and ground finely, add 1 penny weight of aged tea powder, mix well. Each dose is half a penny weight, boiled with a small cup of water and a little honey, then strained and taken warm. After taking, one should calm down and be able to sleep; sweating will promote recovery.

There’s another method with burned fu powder; take small amounts with wine for frequent dosing to encourage sweating and healing. It is especially suitable for timid children.[78p]

　　玉女散　治伤寒，汗后潮热日发，诸药不效。　　川乌一两，火炮去皮脐
　　右为细末，每服一钱或半钱，水一盏半，入生姜一片，枣一枚，煎至四分，温服无时。
　　人参化风膏　治风癎发搐，涕咳无时。　　天麻一两，酒浸　全蝎十四个，微炒　僵蚕微炒　人参　川芎　白附子各半两　羌活　独活　防风各一钱　　右为细末，炼蜜丸如皂子大，每服一丸，荆芥汤化下，量大小与之，无时。
　　黑龙散　治小儿伤寒在表，服冷药，寒伏于中，危困不得汗。　　麻黄　竹茹　苏木　乌龙土乃火团也，各一分　蝎梢二十一个　　右为末，每服半钱，水五分，煎至三分，温服无时。
　　　　单方

　　治小儿伤寒：用葛根汁、淡竹沥各六合，相和，二三岁儿分三服，百日儿斟酌服。 【《千金方》，下同】
　　治小儿时气，桃叶三两捣，以水五升，煮十沸，取汁，日五六遍淋之；若复发烧，雄鼠屎二枚，水调服之。[79p]

Jade Maiden Powder: For treating febrile disease, with tidal fever after sweating, and other medicines proving ineffective: One liang of Chuan Wu, with skin and navel removed, ground into a fine powder. Take one or half qian, with one and a half bowls of water, add a slice of fresh ginger and a jujube, decoct until reduced to a quarter, and take warm at any time.

Ginseng Wind-Resolving Ointment: For treating wind-induced convulsions, with unceasing nasal discharge and coughing: One liang of Tian Ma soaked in wine, fourteen whole scorpions slightly stir-fried, slightly stir-fried silkworms, half a liang each of ginseng, Chuan Qiong, and Bai Fu Zi, each one qian of Qiang Huo, Du Huo, and Fang Feng. Grind into a fine powder, then form it into pills the size of a soap ball. Take one pill with Jing Jie decoction at any time.

Black Dragon Powder: For treating children’s febrile disease present on the surface, where cold medicine has been taken, causing cold to lurk within and preventing sweating: One fen each of Ma Huang, Zhu Ru, Su Mu, and Wu Long Tu (a fire-like substance), and twenty-one scorpion stingers. Grind into powder, with each dose half a qian, mix with five fen of water, decoct until reduced to three fen, and take warm at any time.

Single Recipe: For treating children's febrile disease: use six parts of kudzu root juice and light bamboo juice, mix well, and administer in three doses for children two to three years old, adjusting the dosage for infants under a hundred days.

For treating children's seasonal fevers: three taels of peach leaves pounded, boiled in five sheng of water until it has boiled ten times, strain the juice, and apply it five to six times daily; if the fever recurs, dissolve two pieces of male rat droppings in water and administer.[79p]

　　小儿流涕是风寒也。白芷末、葱白，捣丸小豆大，每茶下二十丸；仍以白芷末，姜汁调涂太阳穴，乃食热葱粥取汗汁。【《圣惠方》】
　　治小儿吹乳胃寒：白豆蔻仁、缩砂仁各十四个，生甘草、炙甘草各二钱为末，常掺入儿口中。【《得效方》】
　　小儿风寒烦热，有疾不省人事：荆芥穗半两焙，麝香、片脑各一字为末，每茶服半钱。大人亦治。【《普济方》】
　　小儿春月外感风寒：用防风、陈皮各三分。羌活、苏叶各二分，蝉壳三只，甘草一分，葱白一寸，生姜一片，煎热服取汗。【《穷乡便方》】
　　小儿伤寒，百日内患壮热：用铁铧一斤烧赤，水二斗，淬三七次，煎一半，入柳叶七片，浴之。【《圣济录》】
　　小儿风寒：萝卜子生研末一钱，温葱酒服之，取微汗大效。 【《卫生易简方》】
　　治伤寒时气，头痛不可忍：以(石卜)硝研细末，油调涂顶上。【《卫生总微》，下同】[80p]

  • When a child has a runny nose, it is due to wind and cold. Grind white atractylodes and scallion whites into a powder, make small balls the size of a broad bean, and have the child take twenty balls with tea. Additionally, apply a paste of white atractylodes and ginger juice to the temples, and then consume hot scallion porridge to induce sweating.

  • To treat a child's cold from nursing: Take fourteen each of white cardamom seeds and small amomum seeds, and two qian each of raw and roasted licorice; grind into a powder and regularly sprinkle it into the child's mouth.

  • For a child experiencing wind-cold with fever and unresponsive state: Roast half a liang of schizonepeta spikes, and grind together with one character each of musk and bezoar into a powder. Administer half a qian with tea. This is also applicable for adults.

  • In the spring, if a child catches wind-cold: Use three fen each of saposhnikovia and dried citrus peel, two fen each of angelica and perilla leaves, three pieces of cicada shell, one fen of licorice, one inch of scallion white, and one slice of fresh ginger; decoct and take hot for sweating.

  • For a child with a cold, suffering from high fever for a hundred days: Burn one jin of iron tridents until red, add two dou of water; quench it seven times, then boil down to half and add seven pieces of willow leaves for bathing.

  • For a child with wind-cold: Grind one qian of radish seeds into a fine powder and take it with warm scallion wine to induce slight sweating with great effect.

  • To treat colds with strong symptoms and unbearable headaches: Grind (stone salt) into a fine powder and mix with oil to apply to the top of the head.[80p]

　　治伤寒毒攻手足痛者：以羊桃汁，杂盐豉汁渍之。
　　治伤寒，因饮水，心下结痞硬痛，名水结。以芫花酢拌，慢火炒熟，用绵裹熨之，冷即易，再炒用，以效为度。
　　治伤寒热毒乘心，神志冒闷，烦躁昏乱：以蓝靛一字或半钱，新水调下。
　　治伤寒，阴证厥逆，以茱萸半升，酒和匀湿，用绢袋二枚盛蒸，令热甚，以熨脚心，冷即易之。候气通畅匀暖，即止。
　　治伤寒，汗后余热不退，烦躁发渴，四肢无力，不能食；以牛蒡根杵烂，绞取汁服，看大小多少与之。
　　　　医案

　　万氏《幼科发挥》曰：一小儿外感风邪，服表散之剂，汗出作喘，此邪气去而脾肺虚也，用异功散而汗喘止，再剂而乳食进。
　　薛铠《保婴撮要》曰：一小儿九岁，素恶风寒，饮食少思，至秋冬口鼻吸气，阴冷至腹，手足如冰，饮姜汤及烧酒方快，其脉细微，两尺如无。余谓此禀命门火衰也，用还少丹不应，改用八味丸，旬余，诸证即愈。[81p]

To treat the pain in the hands and feet caused by febrile illness: use goat-peach juice mixed with salt and fermented soy sauce to soak.

To treat febrile illness causing hardness and pain in the epigastric region due to water retention, known as "water knot": mix garden balsam flower with vinegar, stir-fry over low heat until cooked, wrap in cotton to apply, and change when it cools. Stir-fry again and use as needed.

To treat febrile illness with heat toxin affecting the heart, leading to confusion and restlessness: use indigo dye, one character or half a coin's worth, mixed with fresh water.

To treat febrile illness with Yin syndrome showing reverse cold, use half a sheng of evodia fruit, mixed with wine, and steam in two silk bags until very hot, applying to the soles of the feet. Change when it cools. Wait until the breath is smooth and warm, then stop.

To treat febrile illness with lingering heat after sweating, causing restlessness, thirst, and weakness in the limbs, resulting in inability to eat: pound burdock root into a mash, extract the juice, and administer based on size and quantity.

Medical Case

In Wan's "Developments in Pediatric Studies," it is stated: A child of small stature caught a wind pathogen, took an exterior dispersant and began to sweat and wheeze; once the pathogen was expelled, the spleen and lungs became weak. The treatment with Yigong Powder halted the sweating and wheezing. After another dosage, the child resumed eating.

In Xue Kai's "Essentials for Infant Care," it is mentioned: A nine-year-old child, who has always been sensitive to wind and cold with little appetite, experiences cold air entering the mouth and nose in autumn and winter, leading to chilly sensations in the abdomen and ice-cold hands and feet. Drinking ginger soup and strong liquor provided relief, but the pulse was thin and weak, and the two wrists felt almost absent. I diagnosed this as a deficiency of the fire of the Mingmen. Using Huanshaodan was ineffective, so I changed to Bawei Pill. After about ten days, all symptoms improved.[81p]

　　吴江史安卿子伤风　用表散化痰之药，反痰盛咳嗽，肚腹膨大，面色晃白，此脾土虚不能生肺金也，余用六君子汤加桔梗一剂顿愈。至三日，前证仍作，鼻中流涕；此复伤风寒所致，仍用前药加桑皮、杏仁、桔梗而愈。
　　史少参季子喘嗽，胸腹膨胀，泄泻不食，此饮食伤脾土而不能生肺金也，用六君子汤一剂，诸证悉愈。
　　史木川子六岁感冒咳嗽，发散过度，喘嗽不食，用六君子汤加桔梗而愈。时四月，随其父巡视耕种，忽发寒战，仍复咳嗽，或用发表之剂，痰中有血。余曰：此成肺痈也。次日吐痰兼脓，用桔梗汤而愈。后元气未复，大便似痢，或用五苓、黄连、枳实之类，痰喘目札，四肢抽搐。余曰：此脾气败而变慢脾风也。辞不治，果然。
[82p]

Wujiang's Shi Anqing's son suffered from a cold. After using a medicine to disperse and transform phlegm, he experienced an increase in phlegm and cough, with a swollen abdomen and pale complexion. This indicated that the spleen's deficiency could not generate the lung's essence. I administered a dose of the Six Gentlemen Decoction with added Platycodon and he recovered immediately. However, after three days, the previous symptoms returned, with a runny nose; this was again caused by a cold, so I used the previous medicine with added Mulberry Bark, Apricot Kernel, and Platycodon, leading to recovery.

Shi Shaocan's son had wheezing and coughing, along with an expanded chest and abdomen, diarrhea, and poor appetite. This was due to dietary harm to the spleen's essence, which could not produce the lung's essence. I prescribed one dose of the Six Gentlemen Decoction, and all symptoms were resolved.

Shi Muchuan, aged six, caught a cold and had a cough. After excessive dispersing, he experienced wheezing and loss of appetite. I used the Six Gentlemen Decoction with additional Platycodon and he recovered. It was April, and while accompanying his father inspecting the fields, he suddenly developed chills and resumed coughing. Although some used a medicine to dispel the cold, there was blood in the phlegm. I indicated this was a result of lung abscess. The next day, he coughed up phlegm with pus and recovered after using Platycodon Decoction. Later, his vitality had not fully returned; his bowel movements resembled dysentery, and he sometimes used Five-Ingredient, Coptis, and Bitter Orange preparations. With symptoms of phlegm and wheezing, and extremities twitching, I concluded this was due to weakened spleen qi transforming into chronic spleen wind. He refused treatment, and this indeed was the case.[82p]
